CITY OF SAN MATEO
City Council Regular Meeting
August 15, 2022
7:00 PM
City Hall Council Chamber
330 West 20  Avenue
San Mateo  CA 94403
COUNCIL MEMBERS
Rick Bonilla, Mayor
Diane Papan, Deputy Mayor
 Joe Goethals
Amourence Lee
Eric Rodriguez
AGENDA
THIS MEETING IS BEING HELD PURSUANT TO THE GOVERNOR’S EXECUTIVE ORDERS
WHICH SUSPEND CERTAIN REQUIREMENTS OF THE BROWN ACT.
THIS MEETING CAN BE ATTENDED IN PERSON OR REMOTE BY JOINING ZOOM – SEE CODES BELOW. PUBLIC 
COMMENTS WILL BE ACCEPTED BOTH IN PERSON AND REMOTELY.
SEE END OF AGENDA FOR OPTIONS AND INSTRUCTIONS ON HOW TO PARTICIPATE IN THE MEETING. 
To join via Zoom – click here: August 15, 2022
To join via telephone:  (408) 638-0968      
Webinar ID: 894 8100 0499     Passcode: 099084
The City Council meeting will conclude by 11:00 p.m. unless otherwise extended by council vote. 
Any unheard items will automatically move forward to the next regular meeting. 
CALL TO ORDER
Pledge of Allegiance
Roll Call
CEREMONIAL
1.
Safe from Wildfires Presentation – California Department of Insurance
2.
San Mateo Area Chamber of Commerce Update
CONSENT CALENDAR
All matters listed under the Consent Calendar are considered by the Council to be routine and will be enacted by one motion without
discussion. If discussion is desired, that item may be removed and considered separately.
3.
City Council Meeting Minutes - Approval
Approve the minutes of the City Council Special and Regular meetings of April 18, 2022, May 2, 2022, May 16,
2022, June 6, 2022, June 20, 2022 and July 18, 2022 and the Special meeting minutes of May 23, 2022.
4.
Sustainability & Infrastructure Appointment Subcommittee – Appointment Recommendation
At the recommendation of the Appointment Subcommittee, appoint Sigalle Michael to the Sustainability &
Infrastructure Commission vacancy for a full first term ending on June 10, 2026, and place Pam Rittelmeyer on
the eligibility list, should another vacancy occur.
5.
League of California Cities Annual Conference – Voting Delegate Designation
th
1 of 461

--- page 2 ---
Designate Mayor Rick Bonilla as the City's Voting Delegate for the 2022 League of California Cities Annual
Conference and authorize him to vote for the League’s bylaws amendments.
6.
“Minimum Wage” Amendments – Ordinance Adoption
Adopt an Ordinance to amend Municipal Code Chapter 5.92 “Minimum Wage” to add a Consumer Price Index
percentage cap, a catch-up provision, and round the minimum wage to the nearest five cents.
7.
National Opioid Litigation and Settlement Agreements – Direct Settlement Funds to San Mateo County
Authorize the City Manager and City Attorney to take all necessary steps and execute appropriate documents to
direct settlement funds from the Opioid Settlement Agreements with Distributors and Janssen to San Mateo
County for the duration of both agreements, in the approximate amount of $820,000, and confirm staff action to
direct the first-year payment of Distributor settlement funds in the amount of $28,464.21 to the County.
8.
San Mateo County Mobile Health Clinic – License Agreement
Approve a License Agreement with County of San Mateo to allow a Mobile Health Clinic to operate in the City’s
public right-of-way and authorize the City Manager to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
9.
360 1st Avenue – Lease Amendment
Approve an amendment to the lease for 360 1st Avenue in the Main Street Garage with A+ Mailboxes & More
allowing for a one-year lease extension and an additional one-year option and authorize the City Manager to
execute the lease in substantially the form presented.
10.
Bulk Mailing and Printing – Agreements
Approve bulk mailing and printing services agreements with: 1) CMG Language Services, LLC DBA ColorPrint; and
2) AMS Systems, Inc. DBA AMS Printing, each for an amount not to exceed $150,000 annually;  with each
agreement providing for two 1-year extension options for up to $150,000 each year, for a total not to exceed
amount of $450,000 for each agreement; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreements in
substantially the form presented and to exercise the extension options for each agreement.
11.
Revision of Interim Child Care Fund Guidelines – Approval
Approve the revisions of the Interim Child Care Fund Guidelines.
12.
East Hillsdale Park Construction Drawings – Agreement
Approve an agreement with Callander Associates Landscape Architecture (CALA) to provide professional design
refinement, construction document preparation, bid assistance, and construction observation services for East
Hillsdale Park in the amount of $167,380 with a contingency of $15,000 and authorize the Parks and Recreation
Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
13.
Classification Updates – Police Department
Adopt a Resolution to approve: 1) the job specification and salary range for the new classification of Crime and
Intelligence Analyst; and 2) reallocate 1.0 vacant Management Analyst II position to 1.0 Crime and Intelligence
Analyst position in the Police Department.
14.
Cannabis Tax Fund Grant Program – Appropriation and Agreement
2 of 461

--- page 3 ---
Adopt a Resolution to appropriate funds for the Department of California Highway Patrol Cannabis Tax Fund
Grant Program grant totaling $31,159.32; and authorize the Police Chief to execute the agreement in
substantially the form presented and expend the funds.
15.
Cellebrite Premium Software Subscription – Agreement and Appropriation
Approve an agreement for purchase of Cellebrite Premium Unlimited Software subscription from Cellebrite, Inc.
in the amount of $92,715.35, bringing the cumulative amount to be spent with the vendor for fiscal year 2022-23
to $113,000, and authorize the Chief of Police to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented; and
adopt a resolution approving a fiscal year 2022-23 budget appropriation in the amount of $92,715.35 with a net-
zero impact to the general fund.
16.
Library Materials Acquisition – Agreement
Authorize the Library to spend up to $500,000 annually for fiscal years 2022-23 and 2023-24 in accordance with
terms of the Baker & Taylor agreement approved by the City Council on August 17, 2021, to provide books and
audiovisual materials and with the option to renew for up to three additional years. 
17.
Wastewater Treatment Plant On-Call Consulting Services – Agreements
Approve two on-call professional services agreements for the Wastewater Treatment Plant related services to
Carollo Engineers, Inc. and Brown and Caldwell, with each agreement in the amount of $400,000 for three years,
with two (2) one-year extension options for up to $100,000 per year, for a maximum of five (5) years and
$600,000 for each agreement; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreements substantially
in the form presented, to issue project-specific task orders under these agreements, and to amend the
agreements within the budget amount.
18.
High Voltage Streetlight Conversion (Phase 3) – Agreements
Approve an agreement with St. Francis Electric, LLC for construction of the High Voltage Streetlight Conversion
(Phase 3) Project in the amount of $2,352,230; establish a contingency reserve of $240,000; approve an
agreement with Ghirardelli Associates, Inc. for construction inspection support in the amount of $92,243;
establish a contingency reserve of $9,300; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreements in
substantially the form presented and issue change orders or amendments within the budget and contingency
reserve.
19.
Use of Public Right-of-Way – Agreement
Approve a Utility Equipment Agreement (UEA) with Bandwidth IG, LLC for the construction, installation,
maintenance, and operation of fiber optic network facilities within the public right-of-way and authorize the
Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form attached.
20.
Temporary Standby Generator for Dale Avenue Pump Station Upgrade – Agreement
Approve an Agreement with Herc Rentals, Inc. for a temporary standby generator required to support the Dale
Avenue Pump Station Upgrade project in an amount not-to-exceed $222,090.41 for an estimated period of ten
months; establish a contingency reserve of $110,046; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the
agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency amount.
21.
Collection System Construction Management Services for the Clean Water Program – Amendments
Approve amendments with two professional services firms, Tanner Pacific, Inc. and Townsend Management, Inc.,
to expand the scope of as-needed construction management services under the Clean Water Program to include
support for Wastewater Treatment Plant projects; amend the durational term of the agreements and indemnity
3 of 461

--- page 4 ---
provisions; maintain the originally approved not-to-exceed amounts of $3,000,000 each; and authorize the Public
Works Director to execute the amendments substantially in the form presented and approve future amendments
within the approved budget.
22.
2021 San Mateo Rail Corridor Transportation Management Association – Annual Report
Review and accept the 2021 San Mateo Rail Corridor Transportation Management Association Annual Report.
PUBLIC COMMENT
Members of the public wishing to comment on any item not appearing on the agenda may address the City Council at this time. State
law prevents Council from taking action on any matter not on the agenda; your comments may be referred to staff for follow up.
Public comment is limited to a total of 15 minutes; however, an opportunity for additional public comment may be provided later in
the agenda.
 
NEW BUSINESS
23.
Disposable Food Service Ware Ordinance – Amendment
Introduce an Ordinance to amend San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 5.89 “Disposable Food Service Ware
Ordinance” to recodify a hardship exemption and eliminate duplicative language, to correct a clerical error.
REPORTS AND ANNOUNCEMENTS
City Manager, City Attorney and Council Members report on their various assignments and liaison roles and Council requests for
scheduling future items.
 
ADJOURNMENT
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
AGENDAS: Agendas and material are posted on the City’s website on the Friday preceding each Council Meeting and can be viewed on the City's
website at www.cityofsanmateo.org (https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/) . Any supplemental material distributed to the Council after the posting of
the agenda will be made part of the official record.
WATCHING A MEETING ON TV: City Council meetings are broadcast live on Comcast/channel 27, Wave/channel 26, or AT&T/channel 99.
For transmission problems during the broadcast, please call (650) 522-7099. For all other broadcast comments, call (650) 522-7040, Monday-Friday,
8 a.m. - 5 p.m.
WATCHING A MEETING ON A COMPUTER: There are three ways to stream.
1) Public Meeting Portal www.cityofsanmateo.org/publicmeetings (https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/3971/Agendas-Minutes-Public-Meeting-
Portal)
2) City YouTube channel and stream it on YouTube: http://youtube.com/CityofSanMateo (https://www.youtube.com/user/CityofSanMateo)
3) Watch TV live stream: https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/193/Channel-San-Mateo-Live-Stream (https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/193/Channel-
San-Mateo-Live-Stream) 
PUBLIC COMMENTS/REQUEST TO SPEAK
Prior to the Meeting 
Send comments to: clerk@cityofsanmateo.org until 4 p.m. the day of the meeting.
During the meeting
By Zoom: Click the link at the top of the agenda and you’ll be added to the meeting. All attendees are muted by default. When the item of interest
is open for consideration, select the “Raise Your Hand” icon and you will be called on at the appropriate time.
By telephone: Call (408) 638-0968 and enter the conference ID found at the top of the meeting agenda. When the item of interest is open for
consideration, select *9 to raise your hand. When called upon, press *6 to unmute, state your name and provide your comments.
In Person: At the meeting complete a “Request to Speak” form, submit a request at the speaker kiosk or scan the QR code.
ACCESSIBILITY: In compliance with the Americans with Disabilities Act, those with disabilities requiring special accommodations to participate in
this meeting may contact the City Clerk’s Office at (650) 522-7040 or clerk@cityofsanmateo.org . Notification 48 hours prior to the meeting will
enable the City to make reasonable arrangements to ensure accessibility to this meeting.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
Special Meeting Minutes
City Council
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
April 18, 2022
Remote 5:30 PM
Special Meeting
CALL TO ORDER - This meeting was held pursuant to authorization from Government Code 54943(b)(3) / AB361 (2021) 
in which Brown Act regulations are relaxed to allow members to participate virtually due to the Covid-19 health 
emergency.
Roll Call
Remote:
Mayor Bonilla, Deputy Mayor Papan, Council Members: Lee, Goethals and Rodriguez
STUDY SESSION 
1.
Fiscal Year 2021-22 Mid-Year Budget Update and Fiscal Year 2022-23 Budget Preview
Rich Lee, Finance Director, provided a presentation and overviewed the 2021-22 budget end of year estimates of 
financial position of the City. He reported on impacts from key revenue sources and reviewed recommended uses 
of remaining fund balance. He also provided a 2022-23 preview of the next budget year highlighting projected 
property taxes, sales taxes, real property transfer taxes, and reviewed general fund expenditure assumptions. 
Public Comment – Rich Hedges commended Rich Lee for making the budget understandable. Council also 
commended the financial leadership and the hard work of the Finance team.
2.
Clean Water Program – Water Reuse Update
Azalea Mitch, Public Works Director, presented information on the Clean Water Program's water reuse efforts, 
highlighting types of water reuse, options to offset drinking water demand, water supply resiliency and potential 
next steps. Council asked questions of staff. Public Comment – Drew asked about additional use of purple pipe to 
additional locations.
Council expressed appreciation for the creative and innovative efforts to manage water use resiliency and 
applauded the possible creation of 10 million gallons of water per day. Questions were asked about the availability 
of grant money for some of these efforts. Public Works Director Mitch responded that this document will set us up 
for additional funding sources.
ADJOURNMENT – The meeting adjourned at 6:16 p.m.
APPROVED BY:                                                        
SUBMITTED BY:
Rick Bonilla, Mayor                                                   
Patrice M. Olds, City Clerk

3.
City Council Meeting Minutes - Approval
Approve the minutes of the City Council Special and Regular meetings of April 4, 2022. 
4.
Ordinance Adoption – Sign Code Amendments
Adopt an Ordinance to amend San Mateo Municipal Code Title 25, “Signs” by updating definitions, 
revising regulations for signs in the public right of way, clarifying the permissible number and 
dimensions of signs, and making other miscellaneous changes.
Enactment:  Ordinance No. 2022-04
5.
Remote Teleconferenced City Council and Commission Meetings – Reauthorization
Adopt a Resolution to reauthorize remote teleconferenced City Council and Board and Commission 
meetings for 30 days, through May 18, 2022, as allowed by Assembly Bill 361 amending the Brown Act, 
based upon the Governor’s emergency proclamation and findings that meeting in person would present 
imminent risks to the health or safety of attendees.
Enactment:  Resolution No. 45 (2022)

6.
US 101/State Route 92 Area Improvement and Multimodal Project – Letter of Support
Authorize Mayor Bonilla to send a letter of support on behalf of the City of San Mateo to 
Congresswoman Speier for the San Mateo County Transportation Authority's request for Community 
Project Funding.
7.
On-Call Traffic Engineering Data Collection Services – Amendment
Approve Amendment No. 1 to the agreement with Innovative Data Acquisitions, LLC dba IDAX Data 
Solutions for on-call traffic engineering data collection services in the amount of $110,000 for a new 
agreement total of an amount not to exceed $200,000, extend the term of the agreement, authorize the 
Public Works Director to execute term extension amendments within the agreement amount, and 
authorize the Public Works Director to execute Amendment No. 1 in substantially the form approved.
8.
Wastewater Treatment Plant Immediate Action Projects, Package II – Amendment
Approve Amendment No. 5 to the agreement with Stantec Consulting Services, Inc., to provide 
professional design services and engineering services during construction for Immediate Action Projects 
Package II in the amount of $88,673.46, revising the total agreement amount not to exceed 
$1,562,403.46, extend the term through September 15, 2022, and authorize the Public Works Director 
to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented.
9.
Rodder Truck and Vac-Con Truck – Purchase Contracts
Adopt a Resolution to approve an alternative purchasing procedure and approve a contract with 
National Auto Fleet Group for the purchase of one Rodder Truck from Nixon-Egli Equipment Company 
for $271,665.51 and one Vac-Con Combination Sewer and Storm Drain Cleaner from Vac-Con Inc. for 
$588,981.10, for a total purchase amount of $860,646.61, and authorize the Public Works Director to 
execute the purchase contracts in substantially the form presented.
Enactment:  Resolution No. 46 (2022)
10.
Program for Arterial System Synchronization Fiscal Year 2021-22 Cycle – Funding Agreement
Approve a Joint Funding Agreement with Metropolitan Transportation Commission for the Program for 
Arterial System Synchronization Fiscal Year 2021-22 Cycle, approve matching funds from the City in the 
amount of $7,747, and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the Agreement in substantially 
the form approved.
11.
Central Park Seasonal Ice Rink – Agreement
Approve a five-year zero cost / zero revenue license agreement with On Ice LLC to operate a seasonal ice 
rink in Central Park and authorize the Director of Parks and Recreation to execute the agreement in 
substantially the form presented.
12.
San Mateo Public Library Foundation Operating Lease – Amendment
Approve an amendment to the Property Lease and Operating Agreement with the San Mateo Public 
Library Foundation to extend the lease for an additional year commencing retroactively to April 1, 2022 
through March 31, 2023, and authorize the City Librarian to execute the amendment.
13.
San Mateo City Employees' Association Memorandum of Understanding – Amendment
Adopt a Resolution to amend the Memorandum of Understanding with the San Mateo City Employees' 
Association for salary increases and a term through June 22, 2024.
Enactment:  Resolution No. 47 (2022)

14.
General Fund Unassigned Fund Balance – Commitment Approval
Adopt a Resolution to authorize the commitment of $5,500,000 of General Fund unassigned fund 
balance for negotiated increases to employee compensation and $4,500,000 for capital improvement 
projects.
Enactment:  Resolution No. 48 (2022)

Mack E. Mickelson Arthritis and Rehabilitation Center Therapy Pool – Resolution in Support
Adopt a Resolution to call upon Sutter Health to reopen the Mack E. Mickelson Arthritis and 
Rehabilitation Center Therapy Pool located at the Mills Health Center in San Mateo for community use.
Enactment:  Resolution No. 49 (2022)
PUBLIC COMMENT
Public Comment – Mike Schrader commented on the Mickelson therapy pool needs and requested the issue of the pool 
be taken up by the Senior Citizens Commission to look at senior services. Shawn Leong, Owner of Ah Sam Floral Company 
in San Mateo, inquired how he could utilize his property at 2635 Palm Place for low-income housing. He was invited to 
comment on the General Plan Item #16.
OLD BUSINESS
16.
General Plan Update – Selection of the Preferred Land Use and Circulation Scenario
Zach Dahl, Community Development Deputy Director, introduced the history of the general plan process and 
overviewed prior presentations and outreach efforts. Joanna Jansen, PlaceWorks Consultant, presented the Land 
Use alternatives. Council announced they would take up each Land Use alternative one at a time with a separate 
vote. Council asked questions of staff. 
Public Comment (26) – 1) Raayan Mohtashemi is in favor of Circulation Alternative C. 2) Michael Weinhauer, 
SMRG, commented on Measure Y’s intent to protect from a sham General Plan process. 3) Maxine Terner 
commented on public comment over the holiday weekend and she does not support land use alternative C. 4) 
Charity Wagner suggested modifying certain areas to medium density. 5) Lisa Diaz Nash recommend land use 
alternative A. 6) Ali Sapirman, Housing Coalition, is in strong support of mixed-use high density. 7) Bradley 
Karvasek, Vice President of Development at PS Business Parks, submitted a letter in favor of mixed-use density for 
their site. 8) Gustavo Hornos is in opposition to zoning proposed on his parcel. 9) Dusan Miletich stated in regard 
to study area 9, he sent a letter asking for medium residential designation not low. 10) Laurie Watanuki is in favor 
of alternative A. 11) Martin Wiggins commented that this process has been thorough, done in good faith and easy 
to follow and he supports the circulation option. 12) Chris Conway noted that no demographics were given in the 
survey. 13) David Bohannon spoke of the downshift in the retail business and elaborated on his reasoning for 
mixed use, medium and high density for the Hillsdale site. 14) Ken Chan stated he works on quality affordable 
homes, and would remove land use A from consideration. 15) Erika Powell expressed appreciation for the hard 
work and commented on the language used to describe alternative A. 16) Mike Dunham, Peninsula for Everyone, 
noted he advocates for affordable and sustainable housing. 17) Shawn is concerned with missing input in this 
process from businesses during covid. 18) Jordan Grimes, Peninsula for Everyone, strong support for Alternative C. 
19) Ken Abreu supports Planning Commission’s recommendations. 20) Jennifer Renk, Land Use Counsel for 
Hillsdale Shopping Center, study area number 3 map incorrectly labels PetSmart. It should be mixed-use medium 
not low and that needs a technical correction. 21) Evan Adams supports circulation C and recommends looking at 
Bridgepointe area, concern is lack of transit there. 22) Karen Herrel commented on terminology ‘mixed use’, and 
expressed concerned with EIR. 23) Rich Hedges is in favor of circulation C and land use C. 24) George Derby 
recommends phased approach to implementing general plan guidelines. 25) Laurie Hietter commented on the 
range of growth in the alternatives and concerned with sustainability in growth. 26) Max Mautner stated 
desperately need housing density.

PUBLIC HEARING

Special Meeting Minutes

City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
May 16, 2022
City Hall Council Chambers 5:30 PM
Special Meeting
CALL TO ORDER - This meeting was held pursuant to the Governor’s Executive Orders which suspend certain 
requirements of the Brown Act.
Roll Call
Present:
Mayor Bonilla, Deputy Mayor Papan, Council Members: Goethals and Rodriguez
Remote:
Council Member Lee
STUDY SESSION 
1.
Potential Ballot Measures – Voter Opinion Survey Results
Samantha Weigel, Communications Manager, presented an informational report about the results of a voter 
opinion survey on the feasibility of two potential measures to either increase the City's sales tax rate or make 
changes to the City's existing real property transfer tax. She sought direction on whether to proceed with a 
measure on the November 2022 ballot. Dr. Timothy McLarney, True North Research President, presented the 
results of the Revenue Measure Feasibility Survey and the poll results for a sales tax or Real Property Transfer Tax.
Council asked questions of staff and the consultant.
Public Comment – Raayan Mohtashemi spoke in favor of a revenue measure and stated preference for a sales tax 
measure. 
Council provided comments noting the limited opportunities to generate revenue. Council generally expressed 
mixed feelings on a sales tax measure. After discussion, consensus was in support of a real property transfer tax 
measure for properties in excess of $10 million. Council directed the Finance Director to provide an analysis of 
impacts. Staff indicated the next steps would be drafting potential bond measures for Council to consider.
2.
OneShoreline – Update
San Mateo County Supervisor Dave Pine introduced Len Materman, CEO San Mateo County Flood and Sea Level 
Rise Resiliency District (FSLRRD), who provided a presentation on the OneShoreline initiative. OneShoreline is the 
first independent government agency in California to build resilience to the water-related impacts of climate 
change.  He presented information on the formation of the District and outlined identified programs for the multi-
jurisdictional approach to protect 53 miles of the San Mateo county’s bay shoreline. He noted long-term funding 
sources are needed and the County will be proposing a parcel tax which would be based on a per square foot tax 
(opposite of a regressive tax). Council asked questions and it was noted the longer it takes to start the protection 
measures, the more difficult and expensive it will be. 
Public Comment – Rich Hedges stated funding is also needed for handling flooding of creeks. 
Council Member Papan, FSLRRD board member, stated she is honored to work with both of the presenters and 
thanked them for expressing the risk and the hope to make our communities as resilient as possible.
ADJOURNMENT – The meeting adjourned at 7:00 p.m.

8.
Ordinance Introduction – Access to Reproductive Health Care Facilities
Prasanna Rasiah, City Attorney, provided a presentation explaining the proposed ordinance’s elements which 
would make it unlawful, within 100 feet of reproductive health care facility entrance, to willfully and knowingly 
approach within eight feet of any person or vehicle seeking to enter or exit the facility for the purpose of harassing 
or intimidating a person or vehicle occupants, without their consent. The ordinance also provides rules for 
obstructing access or departure to the facility; complying with law enforcement dispersal orders; and notes that it 
only applies during business hours including one hour before and one hour after regular business hours.
Council asked questions of staff. 
Public Comment – Jessica Dieseldorff, nurse provider, travels to provide abortion services and stated she was very 
alarmed by the experience and trauma of the protestors in front of the San Mateo Planned Parenthood site. Becca 
Horwitz, organizer for Planned Parenthood, appreciated the buffer ordinance. Anticipate massive influx of patients 
in San Mateo because of potential overturn of Roe v. Wade and the City should expect more protestors. Seema 
Patel stated the importance of trauma free access to health providers and inquired how we can communicate to 
people where the 100’ buffer is. Susan Burns, neighbor, stated the harassment is escalating and noted there are 
anti-abortion signs plastered on all the telephone poles and light poles on the street. Jordan Grimes urged 
approval of the ordinance tonight. Ed Callan, Baywood Avenue resident, outlined actions taken to make the street 
safe and hospitable and inquired if the 100’ buffer can be measured by the entrance to the parking lot. Raayan 
Mohtashemi has been chased by an angry protestor. 
Council provided comments in support of this important ordinance to protect people’s rights.
Motion to Introduce an Ordinance to prohibit individuals from harassing, intimidating, or obstructing persons 
seeking access to a reproductive health care facility within 100 feet of an entrance to such a facility. Motion 
passed 5-0.

PUBLIC HEARING 
1.
Draft 2023-2031 Housing Element Public Hearing
Zachary Dahl, Deputy Director, provided a presentation to Council which included an explanation of the 
methodology for estimating development potential for the sites inventory, which is expected to evolve and 
change. He provided an overview of the quantified objectives, and the public outreach and engagement process, 
and further explained how public participation helped influence the development of the Draft Housing Element. 
He noted Diana Elrod, Housing Consultant, was participating remotely and would be available to answer questions 
as needed.
Manira Sandhir, Planning Manager, explained additional required components and goals, policies, and actions; she 
summarized public comments received to date, shared the Planning Commission perspective and reviewed the 
timeline for the process. 
Council asked questions of staff including additional information on the sites inventory methodology, inquired 
about the consultant’s experience and thanked staff for their efforts on preparing the Draft Housing Element. 
Public Comments – Tom Taber supported building more housing and fewer office buildings; Michael from Local 
217 Foster City stated encouraged labor standards and well-paying jobs are needed; Ken Abreu from local chapter 
of the Sierra Club restated elements from submitted letter; Karen Herrel stated concern that there seems to be a 
desire for the Housing Element to fail and why there is still a push for R1 districts; Lisa Diaz Nash supported the 
proposed Housing Element; Jennifer Martinez read remarks from Carol Steinfeld noted the history of racial 
segregation through housing; Noelle Langmack concern that there is no rezoning required to achieve housing 
numbers; Michael Weinhauer stated trickle down housing does not work; Sean stated concern for green space and 
parks in the planning; Karyl Eldridge commented on historical racial issues; Jordan Grimes noted deficiencies with 
lack of rezoning in the element; Justin Alley, One San Mateo, noted the City is not following the law; and Jeremy 
Levine, Housing Leadership Council, noted two letters provided to the City with their recommendations. 
Councilmembers complimented staff on the presentation and follow-up responses to questions, and provided 
individual comments, which included concerns with Commissioner use of their title when providing individual 
comments, review of the demographic trends narrative to ensure that historical segregation and displacement 
were appropriately reflected, the need for more affordable home ownership opportunities, the importance of 
planning for the housing needs of our ‘silver tsunami’ population and homeless population, the importance of 
keeping the Housing Element adoption on schedule to maintain funding opportunities and that staff should 
explore the feasibility of the City achieving a Pro Housing designation from the State.
Staff revisited various comments that were heard to confirm Council consensus on the topics raised, including 
evaluating minimum residential requirements in mixed-use zoning districts, prioritizing senior housing, evaluating 
23 of 461

parking standards for sites near transit, and exploring ways to support non-profits and faith-based organizations 
that want to produce affordable housing.

1.
New State Housing Law Senate Bill 9 (SB9) – Study Session #2
Laura Richstone, Associate Planner, provided a presentation on SB9’s intent and goal to provide additional housing 
to meet demand. She outlined the qualifying criteria and restrictions and reviewed what can be built and updated 
work done since the February 22, 2022 study session. She requested direction on urban lot splits, unit sizes, and 
open space standards. 
Council asked questions of staff and Ms. Richstone and Manira Sandhir, Planning Manager, responded. 
Public Comment – Anne Paulson stated there was a misinterpretation in the Agenda Report and advised the City 
Attorney research. Laurie Watanuki spoke with concern of parking concerns in R1 zones.
Council discussion ensued with individual feedback. Council Member Lee preferred a tiered approach on urban lot 
splits with a cap of four units; creating new FAR standards for SB9 projects; and strongly in favor of open space 
standards. Council Member Rodriguez stated his views are very similar to direction on ADUs and just meet what 
SB9 restricts us to and not press further and he would limit to 2 units per lot; limit to 800 sq ft and allow staff 
discretion as every project and lot is different. He is open to exploring the possibilities for open space standards. 
Deputy Mayor Papan stated limit lot splits to two; allow slightly larger unit size depending on the lot size; and have 
open space standards on the site. Mayor Bonilla stated he is in favor of increasing density and allowing more 
development rather than less and urban lot splits should be allowed; allow larger unit size dictated by the 
underlying zoning; and use of open space standards. 
CLOSED SESSION
Following the opportunity for public comment, there were no speakers, the City Council convened into Closed Session at 
6:34 p.m. to consider:

Code Review

information.

7.50, the City should adopt an impartial hearing officer review procedure with City Council being the final appeal 
body, and City staff should begin work on a draft ordinance to adopt the Dangerous Buildings Code.

22.
Ballot Measure to Increase Existing Real Property Transfer Tax Rate for Properties Sold for $10 Million or More
Samantha Weigel, Communications Manager, provided a presentation on the proposed ballot measure for 
November 8, 2022 to increase Real Property Transfer Tax Rate (RPTT) for properties sold for over $10 Million. She 
outlined the possible revenue and the process. 
Council asked questions of staff.
Public Comment – Lisa Diaz Nash urged the Council to hold off on putting this on the ballot – this is not the time to 
increase taxes on anyone. Raayan Mohtashemi appreciates the simplification of the language and the ballot 
question order.
Council discussion ensued on weighing the timing of introducing a tax while still recovering from the covid 
economic impacts while balancing it against the need for revenue for services that will benefit the San Mateo 
community. Some reservations were expressed; however, it was noted that the Council is putting this in front of 
the voters to ultimately decide. In addition, the need for $300 million in capital improvement projects was 
highlighted and it was further noted the tax has not increased in half a century. Comments were provided by 
Council Members with Rodriguez, Goethals, Lee and Bonilla eventually supporting the measure and Papan stating 
concern because large projects do not always have big users, but many of the mixed-use projects have small users, 
collaborating on a project, who may not have the capability to manage this tax and it may impact projects being 
proposed or completed. This will add on to the cost of the sale and will trickle down to somebody and that may be 
small users. 
Motion to Introduce an Ordinance to amend provisions of Chapter 3.48 “Real Property Document Transfer Tax” of 
the San Mateo Municipal Code to increase the City’s existing real property transfer tax from 0.5% to 1.5% for 
properties sold or transferred for $10 million or more; and adopt a Resolution to call the election and place the 
measure on the November 8, 2022 ballot. Motion passed 4-1.
Moved:
Lee, Seconded: Bonilla
Ayes: 
Bonilla, Lee, Goethals and Rodriguez
Noes: 
Papan
Enactment:  Resolution No. 76 (2022)

would be like. Council had no questions for staff.

membership to provide more data for consideration on this item.

20.
General Plan Update – Land Use Map
Zachary Dahl, Community Development Deputy Director, and Joanna Jansen, PlaceWorks, AICP, LEED AP, Principal, 
provided a presentation on the updated land use maps, in which direction was previously provided at the April 18, 
2022 City Council meeting. Council was asked to provide additional direction on the land use map, heights and 
densities associated with each land use category, and land use designation request for 1501-1555 Hillsdale Blvd. 
Council asked questions of staff.
Public Comment - Gustavo Hornos is concerned with heights. Michael Weinhauer commented on Measure Y; state 
bonus densities should be taken into effect. Ken Abreu, Local Sierra Club Chapter, stated the City is moving in the 
right direction with more density. Bryan Shields, Carpenter's Union 217, look at this as an opportunity to provide 
jobs and add language to General Plan to support prevailing wage and health care pensions. Bradley Karvasek, 
speaking on behalf of PS Business Parks and the owner of Bayshore Corporate Commons, stated they were pleased 
to be designated as mixed-use high site and want to remain mixed-use high. Charity Wagner, speaking on behalf of 
property owners at 1501-1555 West Hillsdale Boulevard, stated this property is underutilized and could increase 
housing. Joe Toscano, Local Union 217, stated interest for adding language for prevailing wages. Michael Ragan 
commented on density and stated don't turn San Mateo into San Francisco. Jordan Grimes supports increasing 5-7 
stories for medium range and 8-12 stories in high range. Raayan Mohtashemi supported the higher range. Taso 
Zografos spoke in support of Measure Y promoting smart growth.
Council discussion ensued. Concerns were expressed about impacts from height proposals and height limits, the 
need to provide for more housing, and opportunities in the transit corridor for density. Discussion ensued with 
regard to properties that flank freeways and what are possible compromises considering Measure Y and Transient 
Oriented Development goals. It was noted the city does not control height and density bonuses as those are set by 
the State and now is the best opportunity to maximize public benefits. There was a desire to check in with the 
community about public benefits. Council Member Rodriguez expressed that 7-8 height limits could become 9-12

scenario A and the other scenarios.

SUBJECT:
League of California Cities Annual Conference – Voting Delegate Designation
RECOMMENDATION:
Designate Mayor Rick Bonilla as the City's Voting Delegate for the 2022 League of California Cities Annual Conference and 
authorize him to vote for the League’s bylaws amendments.
BACKGROUND:
The City is a member of the League of California Cities (League) and as part of its annual conference, a business meeting 
will be conducted on Friday, September 9, 2022 for the League membership to consider and take action on resolutions 
that establish League policy. The City has one vote in the proceedings, and the City Council must designate a voting 
delegate to represent the City and may also appoint up to two alternate voting delegates, one of whom may vote in the 
event the designated voting delegate is unable to serve in that capacity. The form designating the City's voting delegate is 
due to the League no later than September 2, 2022. 
Proposed bylaws amendments will go before the General Assembly for a vote during the 2022 Cal Cities Annual 
Conference. The proposed bylaws amendments can be seen in Attachment 2 to this Agenda Report. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact for taking this action.

direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

All meeting noticing requirements were met.

August 2022 
To: 
Cal Cities General Assembly 
From:  Cindy Silva, President 
Carolyn Coleman, Executive Director and CEO 
Re:       Proposed Cal Cities Bylaws Amendments 
On July 15, 2022, the League of California Cities (Cal Cities) Board of Directors 
(Board) voted to present proposed bylaws amendments to the General Assembly at 
the 2022 Cal Cities Annual Conference and Expo. This memorandum outlines the 
history of the proposed amendments, summarizes the amendments, and provides 
an explanation of the process for adopting amendments to the bylaws.  
Background 
Beginning in 2017, the Board directed Cal Cities to undertake a strategic planning 
process that resulted in the adoption of the “Powering Up for California Cities 
Strategic Grown Plan 2018-2021” (Strategic Growth Plan). The Strategic Growth 
Plan set forth goals to enhance Cal Cities’ governance to: (a) achieve even higher 
levels of engagement and effectiveness; (b) ensure optimal engagement by 
members and effectiveness in supporting fulfillment of the Cal Cities’ mission; 
and (c) ensure the pathway to leadership is transparent and inclusive. 
In furtherance of its governance goals, the Board engaged an association 
governance consultant (Consultant) to evaluate the Cal Cities governance system 
and make recommendations for enhancing Cal Cities’ governance. The Consultant 
gathered and considered input from more than 350 Cal Cities members through 
advisory groups, roundtable discussions, interviews, and surveys. On July 8, 2021, 
the Consultant produced a report (Governance Report) detailing 49 
recommendations to the Board to deepen the engagement of Cal Cities Member 
Cities and ensure Cal Cities’ governance is operating at peak performance.  
The Governance Report included findings indicating that Cal Cities is a strong 
organization, with a high level of member engagement, but also highlighted 
opportunities for Cal Cities to enhance its governance. The opportunities for 
enhancement included: (a) improving the clarity, ease, and consistency in how the 
governance system works; (b) clarifying the guidelines for position qualifications 
and performance expectations; (c) identifying ways to deepen member 
engagement and enhance the quality of the experience of involvement; and (d) 
ensuring Cal Cities has an intentional, consistent organizational culture at all 
levels of the governance system. 
1
52 of 461

--- page 53 ---
The findings and recommendations from the Governance Report were presented to the Board 
during the July 2021 Board meeting. Following a robust exchange of ideas and input, the Board 
decided to move forward with many of the recommendations, referred other recommendations to 
a “to be established” board subcommittee for further study, and deferred consideration of the 
remaining recommendations.  
 
Following Board approval, in September 2021 during the Cal Cities Annual Conference and 
Expo, the General Assembly voted to approve the following bylaws amendments:  
 
1. Adjust the composition of the Board to achieve a higher impact and be more 
representative by adding Director seats to the Board for each of the five Diversity 
Caucuses, and transitioning members of the National League of Cities Board from 
Cal Cities Directors to one non-voting advisor to the Cal Cities Board. 
 
2. Recognize the Cal Cities Diversity Caucuses in the Cal Cities bylaws to reflect 
the full contribution the caucuses make to Cal Cities’ mission and vision. 
 
Those amendments became effective on Nov. 24, 2021. 
 
Among the recommendations the Board decided was a priority to move forward was the 
establishment of a standing Governance Committee to assist the Board in fulfilling its 
governance function.  
 
At its February 2022 meeting, the Board voted to approve Board policy establishing the 
Governance Committee with the task of regularly reviewing the governance structures, policies, 
and practices of Cal Cities and reporting its findings and recommendations to the Board. The 
Board also approved a one-year work plan for the Governance Committee that established 
priority governance issues to focus on in its first year.  
 
Following the Board meeting, President Cindy Silva appointed the following Board members to

The Governance Committee met in April 2022, and following engaging and productive 
discussions, brought forward to the Board at its May 2022 meeting several recommendations to 
further enhance Cal Cities’ governance. Among the recommendations approved by the Board 
during that meeting are two that require bylaws amendments: 
 
1. Formalize oversight of the Resolutions Committee by establishing the Second Vice 
President as the chair of the committee, while retaining the President’s authority to 
appoint the vice chair of the committee.  
 
2. To ensure a more inclusive Nominating Committee, add one committee member 
appointed from among the Caucus Directors and one additional committee member 
appointed from among the At-Large Directors for a total of 13 committee members.1   
 
In addition to those recommendations identified by the Governance Committee and approved by 
the Board, Cal Cities staff identified various non-substantive revisions to the Cal Cities bylaws: 
 
1. Clarify that, unless the Board establishes otherwise, the Cal Cities President appoints 
the chair of Board-established committees.  
 
2. To avoid confusion and clarify organizational responsibilities, remove “Treasurer” from 
the title of the Second Vice President.2   
 
3. To promote consistency, replace the term “Board member(s)” with “Director(s).”3 
 
On July 15, 2022, the Board voted to present these proposed bylaws amendments to the General 
Assembly at the 2022 Cal Cities Annual Conference and Expo. 
 
While the work to enhance Cal Cities’ governance is a process being implemented in phases over 
several years, the Board believes these proposed amendments constitute important next steps 
toward ensuring Cal Cities’ governance is operating at peak performance. 
 
 
 
 
 
1 Under the current bylaws, the Nominating Committee is comprised of 11 Directors. Two committee 
members are appointed from among At-Large Directors and one from a Department. Divisions participate 
on a rotation, with Directors residing within eight of the Divisions appointed in even-numbered years and 
Directors from the other eight appointed in odd-numbered years. 
2 Under the current bylaws, the Second Vice President is referred to as “Second Vice 
President/Treasurer.” However, in practice the Second Vice President does not serve as treasurer of Cal 
Cities. Rather, that function is performed by the Chief Financial Officer designated in Article VIII, 
section 5, subdivision b(2), of the Cal Cities bylaws. 
3 The current bylaws primarily refer to members of the Cal Cities Board of Directors as “Directors.” 
However, there are instances in which they are referred to as “Board members.”

Procedure for Amending the Cal Cities Bylaws 
 
Amendments to the Cal Cities bylaws may be proposed by the Cal Cities Board and may be 
adopted: (a) by vote of the Cal Cities General Assembly, or (b) by mail ballot to Member Cities.4 
In this case, the amendments will be considered by the General Assembly. Bylaws amendments 
need to be approved by 2/3 of those voting,5 and the number that constitutes 2/3 of those voting 
(a) cannot be less than a majority of the voting delegates present if there is a quorum at the time 
the vote is taken;6 or (b) cannot be less than a majority of a quorum if the meeting started with a 
quorum but a quorum is not present when the vote is taken.7 
 
If approved by the General Assembly, the amendments to the bylaws will go into effect after the 
expiration of a 60-day protest period.8 If, within 60 days after the adoption of the amendments, 
one-third or more of Member Cities submit a written protest against such amendments, the 
amendments are automatically suspended until the next Annual Conference and Expo, when they 
may be taken up again for reconsideration and vote.9 If the amendments are approved by the 
General Assembly and no protest is lodged, the effective date of the bylaws amendments will be 
Nov. 9, 2022.

RESOLUTION RELATING TO AMENDMENTS TO THE CAL CITIES BYLAWS 
(2/3 vote at General Assembly required to approve) 
 
 
 
Source:   
League of California Cities Board of Directors 
 
 
WHEREAS, the League of California Cities (Cal Cities) is a nonprofit mutual benefit 
corporation under California law and, as such, is governed by corporate bylaws; and 
 
 
WHEREAS, the Cal Cities Board of Directors (Board) periodically reviews the Cal Cities 
bylaws for issues of clarity, practicality, compliance with current laws, and responsiveness to 
membership needs and interests; and 
 
WHEREAS, beginning in 2017, the Board directed Cal Cities to undertake a strategic 
planning process that resulted in the adoption of the “Powering Up for California Cities Strategic 
Growth Plan 2018-2021” (Strategic Growth Plan); and 
 
WHEREAS, the Strategic Growth Plan set forth goals to enhance Cal Cities’ governance 
to: (a) achieve even higher levels of engagement and effectiveness; (b) ensure optimal 
engagement by members and effectiveness in supporting fulfillment of the Cal Cities’ mission; 
and (c) ensure the pathway to leadership is transparent and inclusive; and 
 
WHEREAS, in furtherance of its governance goals, the Board engaged an expert in 
association governance who gathered and considered input from more than 350 Cal Cities 
members through advisory groups, roundtable discussions, interviews, and surveys to evaluate 
the Cal Cities governance system and make recommendations for enhancing Cal Cities’ 
governance; and 
 
WHEREAS, in July 2021 the Board decided to move forward with certain 
recommendations made as a result of that governance evaluation, including a recommendation to 
establish a standing Governance Committee of the Board to assist the Board in fulfilling its 
governance function; and  
 
WHEREAS, in February 2022 the Board approved Board policy establishing the 
Governance Committee and charging it with regularly reviewing the governance structures, 
policies, and practices of Cal Cities, and reporting its findings and making recommendations to 
the Board; and 
 
WHEREAS, in 2022 the Governance Committee recommended, and the Board, approved 
certain changes to the bylaws that: (1) formalize the oversight of the Resolutions Committee; (2) 
ensure a more inclusive Nominating Committee by adding one committee member appointed 
from among Caucus Directors and one additional committee member appointed from among At-
Large Directors; (3) clarify that, unless the board establishes otherwise, the Cal Cities President 
appoints the chair of board-established committees; and (4) make various non-substantive 
revisions; and

Article VI. Resolutions

Section 3:  Resolutions Committee for Annual Conference Resolutions. 
 
(a) Resolutions Committee Composition.  The Cal Cities President establishes 
a Resolutions Committee sixty days prior to each Annual Conference, which 
committee shall consist of: 
 
(i) One elected official from each regional division, appointed by the 
regional division; 
 
(ii) One elected official from each policy committee, appointed by the 
policy committee; 
 
(iii) One member from each functional department, appointed by the 
department; 
 
(iv) One elected official from each caucus, appointed by the caucus; and 
 
(v) Up to ten additional members (at least five of whom are elected 
officials) as the Cal Cities President deems necessary to achieve 
geographic and population balance, as well as recognize the 
multiplicity of city functions not represented by the other 
appointments, including, but not limited to, the perspectives of board 
and commission members as well as professional staff. 
 
(b) Presidential Appointments.  In the event a regional division, policy 
committee, functional department, or caucus does not make its appointment 
to the Resolutions Committee, the Cal Cities President may make the 
appointment on the regional division’s, policy committee’s, functional 
department’s, or caucus’s behalf. 
 
(c) Chair.  The Cal Cities President shall also appoint to the Resolutions 
Committee a committee chair and vice chairSecond Vice-President shall 
serve as committee chair. The Cal Cities President shall also appoint to the 
Resolutions Committee a vice chair.  
 
(d) Minimum Committee Size and Composition.  In the event the full 
committee is not in attendance at the Annual Conference, the Cal Cities 
President shall appoint a sufficient number of city officials in attendance to 
achieve a total of thirty.  No less than two-thirds of the members of the 
Resolutions Committee shall be elected officials.

Section 2:  Composition. 
 
The Cal Cities Board is composed of the following: 
 
(a) A President, First Vice-President and Second Vice-President/Treasurer, who 
each serve a term of one year; 
 
(b) The Immediate Past President who serves for a term of one year, immediately 
succeeding his or her term as President; 
 
(c) Twelve Directors-at-Large, 
 
(i) Who serve staggered two-year terms, and 
 
(ii) At least one of whom is a representative of a small city with a 
population of 10,000 or less; 
 
(d) One Director to be elected from each of the regional divisions, functional 
departments, and caucuses of Cal Cities, each of whom serves for a term of 
two years; and 
 
(e) Ten Directors that may be designated by the mayors of each of the ten largest 
cities in California to serve two-year terms. 
 
(f) For purposes of this section, the population of each city is the most current 
population as determined by the California Department of Finance, 
Demographic Research Unit, or its successor agency or unit.  If no successor 
agency or unit is named, the most current population used to determine these 
dues shall be used to determine future dues until such time as these bylaws 
are amended to designate a new source for determining city population. 
 
(g) Directors hold office until their successors are elected and qualified.

(a) Timing.  The Cal Cities President, with the concurrence of the Cal Cities 
Board, shall establish a nominating committee at the first Board meeting of 
the calendar year in which the election is to occur. 
 
(b) Composition.  The nominating committee shall be comprised of eleven 
thirteen Board membersDirectors.  ThreeTwo nominating committee

positions on the Cal Cities Board are not eligible to serve on the nominating 
committee.  In the event a regional division representative on the nominating 
committee wishes to be a candidate for an officer or at-large position, the Cal 
Cities President will appoint a substitute nominating committee member from 
the same regional division, if available.  If one is not available, the President 
shall appoint a substitute from a nearby regional division.

Cities officers and at-large board membersDirectors; and 
 
(iii) President and First Vice President Recommendation.  
Recommend whether the previous year’s First Vice President

Section 8:  Meetings and Meeting Notice. 
 
(a) Regularly Scheduled Board Meetings.  The Cal Cities Board shall meet no 
fewer than four times a year.  Notice of regularly scheduled Board meetings 
shall be mailed to each Director at least 14 days before any such meeting. 
 
(b) Emergency Board Meetings.  A good faith effort shall be made to provide 
notice of any emergency board meetings (for example, by first-class mail, 
personal or telephone notification, including a voice messaging system or 
other system or technology designed to record and communicate messages, 
telegraph, facsimile, electronic mail, or other electronic means). 
 
(c) Telephonic or Electronic Participation.  Members of the Cal Cities Board 
may participate in any meeting through the use of conference telephone or 
similar communications equipment, so long as all members participating in 
such meeting can hear one another.  Participation in a meeting by this means 
constitutes presence in person at such meeting. 
 
(d) Notice Content.  All meeting notices shall include the meeting date, place, 
time, and, as applicable, the means by which a Cal Cities Board 
memberDirector may participate electronically.

Section 10:  Committees. 
 
(a) General.  The Cal Cities Board may establish committees to study city 
problems, advise on Cal Cities educational efforts, make recommendations 
with respect to Cal Cities advocacy efforts, or to engage in other appropriate 
Cal Cities service. 
 
(b) Executive Committee. 
 
(i) Composition.  The Executive Committee of the Cal Cities Board 
consists of the following:  the Cal Cities President, First Vice-
President, Second Vice-President/Treasurer, Immediate Past 
President and Executive Director. 
 
(ii) Authority.  The Executive Committee has authority to act for the Cal 
Cities Board between Board meetings, provided that no action of the 
Executive Committee is binding on the Cal Cities Board unless 
authorized or approved by the Board. 
 
(c) Standing Policy Committees. 
 
(i) Charge.  Cal Cities shall have a series of standing policy committees, 
whose charge shall be to make recommendations to the Cal Cities 
Board on matters within the committees’ jurisdiction, as well as fulfill 
other duties specified in these bylaws (see, for example, Article VI, 
section 4(b)). 
 
(ii) Membership.  Each Cal Cities Policy Committee shall be comprised 
of the following: 
 
• Two members appointed by each regional division president; 
 
• One member appointed by each functional department president; 
 
• One member appointed by each caucus president; 
 
• No more than 16 members appointed by the Cal Cities President, 
to provide population and geographic balance, as well as expertise; 
and 
 
• Such representatives of affiliate organizations in the capacity 
authorized by the Cal Cities Board. 
 
(iii) Feedback.  Policy committees shall receive information on actions 
taken on committee recommendations and the reasons for those 
actions.

Article VIII:  Officers 
 
Section 1:  Identity. 
 
The officers of Cal Cities are a President, a First Vice-President, a Second Vice-
President/Treasurer, an Immediate Past President, and an Executive Director. 
 
Section 2:  Duties of Cal Cities Officers. 
 
(a) President.  The President presides at all Cal Cities Board meetings and all 
General Assemblies.  The President has such other powers and duties as 
may be prescribed by these bylaws or the Cal Cities Board. 
 
(b) First Vice-President.  The First Vice-President carries on the duties of the 
President in the President’s temporary absence or incapacity.  The First Vice-
President has such other powers and duties as may be prescribed by these 
bylaws or the Cal Cities Board. 
 
(c) Second Vice-President/Treasurer.  The Second Vice-President/Treasurer 
carries on the duties of the President in the President’s and First Vice-
President’s temporary absence or incapacity.  The Second Vice-
President/Treasurer has such other powers and duties as may be prescribed 
by these bylaws or the Cal Cities Board. 
… 
Section 4:  Vacancies. 
 
A vacancy in the office of President is filled by the Immediate Past President who shall 
serve for the unexpired term of office and, upon election of a new President at the next 
Annual Conference, shall subsequently serve a full term as Immediate Past President. 
In the event the Immediate Past President is not available to fill the vacancy in the office 
of the President, or declines in writing, it shall be filled by the succession of the First 
Vice-President to that office.  A vacancy in the office of First Vice-President, or Second 
Vice-President/Treasurer, is filled for the un-expired term by appointment by the Cal 
Cities Board of a member of the Cal Cities Board.  A vacancy in the office of the 
Immediate Past President is filled for the un-expired term by the last Past President 
continuing to hold a city office.

Article XII: Voting 
… 
Section 5:  Mail Balloting. 
 
In addition to voting at Cal Cities meetings, Cal Cities may solicit member input by mail 
ballot. 
 
(a) Mailing.10  The question(s) to be voted upon, along with explanatory 
materials and a ballot, shall be mailed by first class mail to each Member City 
for consideration and action. 
 
(b) Time Frame for Action.  Member Cities shall have at least 45 days to cast 
their vote.  Ballots shall be cast by returning the Member City’s ballot to Cal 
Cities’ principal office in Sacramento. 
 
(c) Ballot Tabulation and Results Announcement.  The Cal Cities President 
will appoint a counting committee of three board membersDirectors to count 
the votes cast by mail ballot.  The counting committee will submit its count to 
the Cal Cities Board, which shall canvass the vote and announce the results. 
 
(d) Functional Departments, Regional Divisions, and Caucuses.  
Departments, divisions, and caucuses may also use mail balloting under 
procedures specified in their respective bylaws.

Article XV: Prohibited Transactions 
… 
 
Section 4:  Ethical Considerations. 
 
These restrictions, of course, represent the floor, not the ceiling, for ethical conduct as a 
Cal Cities board memberDirector or policy committee member.  If a board 
memberDirector or policy committee member believes that there are circumstances 
under which Cal Cities’ members might reasonably question the board 
member’sDirector’s or policy committee member’s ability to act solely in the best 
interests of Cal Cities and its member cities, the prudent course is to abstain.  As an 
example, typically Cal Cities board membersDirectors have abstained from participating 
in decisions on legislation that would affect organizations for which they work.  Another 
example is legislation that would uniquely benefit a board member’sDirector’s city.  
Policy committee members should also consider abstaining in similar circumstances.

SUBJECT:
“Minimum Wage” Amendments – Ordinance Adoption
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt an Ordinance to amend Municipal Code Chapter 5.92 “Minimum Wage” to add a Consumer Price Index percentage 
cap, a catch-up provision, and round the minimum wage to the nearest five cents. 
BACKGROUND:
On July 18, 2022, the City Council introduced the attached ordinance to amend San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 5.92 
“Minimum Wage” to add a Consumer Price Index percentage cap, a catch-up provision, and round the minimum wage to 
the nearest five cents. Clean and redline versions of the proposed ordinance are attached. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The proposed amendments to the minimum wage ordinance will not have any budget impact as the City hires above the 
minimum wage. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This ordinance introduction is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that 
will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
DRAFT ORDINANCE
Amend Section 5.92.020 of the Municipal Code to Add a Consumer Price Index Percentage Cap, a Catch-up 
Provision, and to Round the Minimum Wage to the Nearest Five Cents.
WHEREAS, Staff presented an informational update on the City’s local minimum wage to the City 
Council; 
WHEREAS, Staff received direction from the City Council to amend the City’s ordinance to align with 
local jurisdictions’ ordinances; 
WHEREAS, the policy direction was to include a Consumer Price Index (CPI) cap to steadily increase the 
minimum wage without negatively impacting small businesses from large increases in any given year. In addition 
to the CPI cap, the City Council directed staff to create a catch-up provision and to round the wage to the 
nearest five cents.
Now, therefore, the Council of the City of San Mateo ordains as follows:
Section 1. Section 5.92.020 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
5.92.020 Minimum Wage.
(a) Employers shall pay employees no less than the minimum wage for each hour worked within the 
geographic boundaries of the City.
(1) For employers which are not non-profit corporations, the minimum wage paid shall be as 
follows:
(2) Beginning January 1, 2017, the minimum wage shall be an hourly rate of $12.00.
(3) Beginning January 1, 2018, the minimum wage shall be an hourly rate of $13.50.
(b) Beginning January 1, 2019, the minimum wage shall be an hourly rate of $15.00.
(1) For employers which are non-profit corporations, the minimum wage rate shall be as follows:
(2) Beginning January 1, 2017, the minimum wage shall be an hourly rate of $10.50.
(3) Beginning January 1, 2018, the minimum wage shall be an hourly rate of $12.00.
(4) Beginning January 1, 2019, the minimum wage shall be an hourly rate of $13.50.
(c) Beginning January 1, 2020, the minimum wage shall be equal to that of the employers which are not 
non-profit corporations, and shall be subject to the Consumer Price Index increase as described in subsection 
(d), with the amount of the Minimum Wage increase rounded to the nearest five cents ($.05).
67 of 461

--- page 68 ---
(d) Beginning on January 1, 2020, and each January thereafter, the minimum wage shall increase by an 
amount equal to the prior year's increase, if any, in the Consumer Price Index (CPI) for San Francisco-Oakland-
San Jose as determined by the United States Department of Labor. The change shall be calculated by using the 
August to August change in the CPI to calculate the annual increase, up to 3.5%, as described in subsection (e). A 
decrease in the CPI shall not result in a decrease in the minimum wage.
(e) Cost of living increases to the Minimum Wage based on the CPI shall not exceed 3.5% annually. 
When the actual CPI exceeds the 3.5% cap, the percentage amount in excess of the cap shall be applied to the 
following year’s CPI increase, up to the 3.5% cap.  Excess amounts shall be carried over from year to year until 
the actual CPI and the cap-adjusted CPI are equivalent.
(f) An employee who is a learner, as defined by California Industrial Welfare Commission Order No. 4-
2001, shall be paid no less than 85% of the applicable minimum wage for the first 160 hours of employment. 
Thereafter, the employee shall be paid the applicable minimum wage rate.
(g) An employer may not deduct an amount from wages due an employee on account of any tip or 
gratuity, or credit the amount or any part thereof, of a tip or gratuity, against, or as a part of, the wages due the 
employee from the employer.
(h) Environmental Determination. In accordance with California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) 
Guidelines, this ordinance introduction is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or 
administrative activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).).
(i) Severability. In the event any section, clause or provision of this Ordinance shall be determined 
invalid or unconstitutional, such section, clause or provision shall be deemed severable and all other sections or 
portions hereof shall remain in full force and effect.
(j) Publication. This Ordinance shall be published in summary in a newspaper of general circulation, 
posted in the City Clerk's Office, and posted on the City's website, all in accord with Section 2.15 of the City 
Charter.
(k) Legislative History and Effective Date. This Ordinance was introduced on Clerk to complete., and 
adopted on Clerk to complete., and shall be effective 30 days after its adoption.

SUBJECT:
National Opioid Litigation and Settlement Agreements – Direct Settlement Funds to San Mateo County
RECOMMENDATION:
Authorize the City Manager and City Attorney to take all necessary steps and execute appropriate documents to direct 
settlement funds from the Opioid Settlement Agreements with Distributors and Janssen to San Mateo County for the 
duration of both agreements, in the approximate amount of $820,000, and confirm staff action to direct the first-year 
payment of Distributor settlement funds in the amount of $28,464.21 to the County. 
BACKGROUND:
On December 6, 2021, the City Council authorized the City Attorney to participate in nationwide opioid settlement 
agreements with three opioid distributors – Cardinal Health, McKesson, and AmerisourceBergen (hereinafter, the 
“Distributors”) and the opioid manufacturer Janssen Pharmaceuticals, Inc., which is owned by Johnson and Johnson 
(collectively, “J&J”). The Council further authorized the signing of implementing State Subdivision Agreements. As stated in 
that report, staff is now returning to the Council for a decision on directing settlement funds to the County. 
The estimated payment is $28,464.21 under the first year of the Distributor settlement agreement.  While the estimated 
payment under the first year of the J&J agreement is currently unknown, our understanding is that the City could receive 
approximately $820,000 in total under both settlement agreements.  Funds under the settlement agreement with the 
Distributors would be distributed to states and local governments over an 18-year period.  The agreement with J&J would 
cover a nine-year period. 
On July 21, 2022, the settlement administrator (BrownGreer, LLC) informed the City that it had until August 5, 2022 to 
decide whether to opt for direct payment or reallocate all or a portion of its payment to San Mateo County. Staff was also 
told that any changes in election would need to be made at least 60 days prior to a payment date, which is not presently 
known. 
After consultation with the County, and given the dollar amount at issue, City staff elected to direct the first-year payment 
of Distributor settlement funds in the amount of $28,464.21 to the County.  Funds going directly to participating states and 
subdivisions must be used for pre-approved purposes designed to help abate the opioid epidemic. These include a wide 
range of intervention, treatment, education, and recovery services. If the City receives a direct payment it is obligated to 
report on the use of the funds, which must be used primarily for opioid abatement. Given that existing County 
infrastructure could be employed to appropriately use these funds, it appeared to staff that it would be more cost-
effective for the County to administer these funds. 
Preliminarily, the County has informed staff that it intends to use opioid settlement funds for several purposes.  These 
include adding onsite medical monitoring to a residential detoxification facility planned for re-opening, and developing a 
69 of 461

--- page 70 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
comprehensive community education and early intervention response.  The County is also proposing to expand 
medication-assisted treatment staffing and services for individuals with opioid and other chronic substance use in areas 
such as jails, homeless shelters, and on the street.      
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact for taking this action as it involves a decision whether to receive direct payments or authorize 
payment of the settlement funds to San Mateo County.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This proposed action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

SUBJECT:
San Mateo County Mobile Health Clinic – License Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve a License Agreement with County of San Mateo to allow a Mobile Health Clinic to operate in the City’s public 
right-of-way and authorize the City Manager to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The San Mateo County Health Department operates a Mobile Health Clinic (Clinic) to offer health care services to 
homeless and uninsured persons. The mobile clinic previously operated at the City’s 5th Avenue and Claremont Street 
parking lot, formerly known as the Worker’s Resource Center parking lot. This parking lot recently closed for construction 
of the future Kiku Crossing Public Garage. 
San Mateo County Health staff contacted the Public Works Department in December 2021 to request assistance in finding 
an alternate location to park and operate the Clinic. Staff identified four on-street parking spaces on Claremont Street 
between 2nd and 3rd Avenues that meet City and Clinic needs, including site visibility, accessibility for pedestrians and 
vehicles, and proximity to the Clinic’s patients. The identified site is located adjacent to 435 East 3rd Avenue, which is 
planned for redevelopment in the coming years. As a result, the term of the agreement is two years, allowing staff to find a 
new location for the clinic prior to the development project moving forward to construction, if approved. 
If the City Council approves the License Agreement, it would allow the Clinic to utilize the identified on-street spaces on 
Tuesdays and Thursdays from 8:30 AM to 3:00 PM, with the clinic opening at 9:30 AM. “No Parking” signs will be posted on 
nearby street poles to discourage public parking at the identified spaces during clinic hours. Based on the foregoing, staff 
recommends approval of the License Agreement to allow the San Mateo County’s Mobile Health Clinic to continue 
providing necessary medical services to the community. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact associated with this agreement.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This License Agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because (1) it can be seen with certainty that there is no 
possibility that the operation of a mobile health clinic may have a significant effect on the environment, and (2) it is an 
organizational or administrative activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA 
Guidelines Sections 15061(b)(3), 15378(b)(5).)

This LICENSE AGREEMENT (“Agreement”) is made as of _______________, 
("Effective Date") by and between the City of San Mateo, a municipal corporation existing under

RECITALS 
 
A. 
Whereas, Licensor is the owner of certain parcel(s) of real property situated in the City of 
San Mateo, California, shown on Exhibit A, attached hereto and incorporated herein by 
reference (the “Property”). 
 
B. 
Whereas, Licensee seeks to use a portion of the Property (hereafter “Licensed Space,” 
depicted on Exhibit A) for a Mobile Health Clinic operated by Licensee’s County Health 
Department. 
 
C. 
Whereas, as consideration and in lieu of a license fee, Licensor has determined the use of 
the Licensed Space for the operation of the Mobile Health Clinic benefits its citizens by  
offering convenient and confidential medical care.   
 
D. 
Whereas, Licensor desires to grant to Licensee a license for access to and use of Licensed 
Space based on the above and subject to the terms and conditions of this License Agreement 
(hereinafter “License” or “Agreement.”) 
 
AGREEMENT 
 
NOW THEREFORE, for good and valuable consideration, the receipt and adequacy of which are 
hereby acknowledged, the parties agree as follows: 
 
1. Grant of License.   
 
Licensor hereby grants to Licensee and its employees, representatives, and contractors, a personal, 
revocable license (“License”) to enter upon the Property to use the Licensed Space to operate a 
Mobile Health Clinic. Licensee, along with its employees, consultants, subcontractors, volunteers 
and/or other persons under its control retained in connection with the operation of the Mobile 
Health Clinic, shall be permitted to use this License unless otherwise prohibited by Licensor. This 
Agreement grants Licensee a license only and notwithstanding anything to the contrary herein, 
this License does not constitute a grant by City of any ownership, leasehold, easement, or other 
property interest or estate whatsoever in the Property, or any portion thereof. Nothing in this 
Agreement shall be construed as granting or creating any franchise rights pursuant to any federal, 
state, or local laws.

2. Conditions of License 
 
a) Licensee shall not store any hazardous materials on the Licensed Space, shall dispose 
of all medical materials off-site, and shall be responsible for repairing any damages to 
the Licensed Space caused by its activities under this Agreement. 
 
b) To minimize public disruptions, the use of the Licensed Space by Licensee is 
restricted and allowed only on weekdays between 7:30 a.m. and 4:00 p.m. Use of the 
Licensed Space by Licensee is not allowed after 4:00 p.m., on weekends, or on City 
Holidays without written approval from the City of San Mateo Department of Public 
Works. 
 
c) Licensee shall ensure its activities do not interfere with the safe flow of pedestrian and 
vehiular traffic as determined by the City.  If the City determines Licensee’s 
operations presents a traffic safety concern, Licensee shall alter its operations upon 
request by the City.   
 
d) Licensee shall ensure all public walkways, sidewalks, or other paths of travel at or 
near the Licensed Space are ADA compliant by ensuring its activities continue to 
allow for a minimum 36-inch width on any public path of travel.  
 
e) Licensee shall document (via photos, videos, etc.) existing condition of site prior to 
utilizing the Licensed Space. Licensee shall transmit these records to Licensor within a 
week of the execution of this Agreement.   
 
f) Licensee shall maintain access to Licensed Space for Licensor at all times.  
 
 
3. Nonexclusivity of License.

Space by Licensor and other parties who may be granted access by Licensor.

be connected with the physical or environmental condition of the Licensed Space and any related 
improvements or any law or regulation applicable thereto or the suitability of the Licensed Space 
for Licensee’s intended use.
