INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS 
 
 
 
A. 
General Liability, Automobile, Worker’s Compensation, and Professional Liability 
 
Licensee shall procure, prior to commencement of service, and keep in force for the term of 
this contract, at Licensee’s own cost and expense, the following policies of insurance or 
certificates or binders as necessary to represent that coverage as specified below is in place 
with companies doing business in California and with AM Best ratings of at least A-VII or 
better. The insurance shall, at a minimum, include: 
 
1. 
 Commercial General Liability insurance. Shall cover liability arising from 
premises, operations, independent contractors, products-completed operations, personal and 
advertising injury, bodily injury, broad form property damage, and liability assumed under an 
insured contract (including the tort liability of another assumed in a business contract). 
 
(a) Coverage afforded on behalf of the Licensor shall be primary insurance and 
any other insurance available to the Licensor under any other policies shall be 
excess insurance (over the insurance required by this Agreement). 
 
(b) Limits of liability: Licensee shall maintain commercial general liability 
(CGL) and, if necessary, commercial umbrella insurance with a limit of not less 
than $2,000,000 each occurrence. 
 
(a)  If the policy is a “claim made” type policy, the following should be included 
as endorsements: 
(i) 
The retroactive date shall be the effective date of this Agreement or a 
prior date. 
(ii)     The extended reporting or discovery period shall not be less 
than thirty-six (36) months. 
 
2. 
Automobile Liability Insurance. Licensee shall maintain automobile 
liability insurance with a limit of not less than $1,000,000 each accident. Such insurance 
shall cover liability arising out of any auto (including owned, hired, and non-owned 
autos). Coverage shall be written on ISO form CA 00 01, CA 00 05, CA  00 12, CA 00 20, or 
a substitute form providing equivalent liability coverage. If necessary, the policy shall be 
endorsed to provide contractual liability coverage equivalent to that provided in the 1990 and 
later editions of CA 00 01. In the event the Licensee does not own vehicles, but utilized non-
owned and hired vehicles, evidence of such coverage is acceptable with a signed statement 
from Licensee stating that only non-owned and hired vehicles are used in the course of the 
contract.

ELECTRONIC RECORD AND SIGNATURE DISCLOSURE 
From time to time, Carasoft OBO County of San Mateo (we, us or Company) may be required by
law to provide to you certain written notices or disclosures. Described below are the terms and
conditions for providing to you such notices and disclosures electronically through your
DocuSign, Inc. (DocuSign) Express user account. Please read the information below carefully
and thoroughly, and if you can access this information electronically to your satisfaction and
agree to these terms and conditions, please confirm your agreement by clicking the 'I agree'
button at the bottom of this document. 
Getting paper copies 
At any time, you may request from us a paper copy of any record provided or made available
electronically to you by us. For such copies, as long as you are an authorized user of the
DocuSign system you will have the ability to download and print any documents we send to you
through your DocuSign user account for a limited period of time (usually 30 days) after such
documents are first sent to you. After such time, if you wish for us to send you paper copies of
any such documents from our office to you, you will be charged a $0.00 per-page fee. You may
request delivery of such paper copies from us by following the procedure described below. 
Withdrawing your consent 
If you decide to receive notices and disclosures from us electronically, you may at any time
change your mind and tell us that thereafter you want to receive required notices and disclosures
only in paper format. How you must inform us of your decision to receive future notices and
disclosure in paper format and withdraw your consent to receive notices and disclosures
electronically is described below. 
Consequences of changing your mind 
If you elect to receive required notices and disclosures only in paper format, it will slow the
speed at which we can complete certain steps in transactions with you and delivering services to
you because we will need first to send the required notices or disclosures to you in paper format,
and then wait until we receive back from you your acknowledgment of your receipt of such
paper notices or disclosures. To indicate to us that you are changing your mind, you must
withdraw your consent using the DocuSign 'Withdraw Consent' form on the signing page of your
DocuSign account. This will indicate to us that you have withdrawn your consent to receive
required notices and disclosures electronically from us and you will no longer be able to use your
DocuSign Express user account to receive required notices and consents electronically from us
or to sign electronically documents from us. 
All notices and disclosures will be sent to you electronically 
Unless you tell us otherwise in accordance with the procedures described herein, we will provide
electronically to you through your DocuSign user account all required notices, disclosures,
authorizations, acknowledgements, and other documents that are required to be provided or
made available to you during the course of our relationship with you. To reduce the chance of
you inadvertently not receiving any notice or disclosure, we prefer to provide all of the required
notices and disclosures to you by the same method and to the same address that you have given
us. Thus, you can receive all the disclosures and notices electronically or in paper format through
the paper mail delivery system. If you do not agree with this process, please let us know as
described below. Please also see the paragraph immediately above that describes the
consequences of your electing not to receive delivery of the notices and disclosures
electronically from us.

City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
City Manager's Department
MEETING DATE:
August 15, 2022 
SUBJECT:
360 1st Avenue – Lease Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an amendment to the lease for 360 1st Avenue in the Main Street Garage with A+ Mailboxes & More allowing for 
a one-year lease extension and an additional one-year option and authorize the City Manager to execute the lease in 
substantially the form presented. 
BACKGROUND:
There are six commercial leases at the Main Street Garage that are owned and managed by the City. The commercial 
spaces were created to attract retail tenants that add amenities to the Downtown.  A+ Mailboxes & More, run by Dylan 
Siddiq, is the City’s tenant in the Main Street Garage at the 360 1st Avenue space. They are a retail pack and ship store 
where customers can rent mailboxes to receive mail and packages. The store also provides auxiliary services such as copy, 
fax, print, notary, passport photo, video transfer, and fingerprint background checks. 
A+ Mailboxes & More has been a tenant at the location since November 2012. Previously, the City has approved several 
three-year lease extensions. Due to the uncertainty of the on-going COVID pandemic, the owner has a requested a one-
year lease extension with an option to renew for an additional year. As small businesses continue to recover from the 
economic impact of the COVID pandemic, the real estate market for retail spaces have remained flat. Consequently, the 
City’s commercial property manager recommends the lease rate remain at $1,201.04 monthly for the next 12 months with 
a 3% increase for the option year.  There is an additional monthly fee of $70.00 for maintenance of common areas. The 
tenant will cover all utilities, taxes, and permits. 
Landlord Concession
Heavy rains between October 2021 and February 2022 caused severe flooding inside the store and necessitated immediate 
emergency mold remediation and removal. The leaks in the Main Street Garage from the rainstorms resulted in business 
interruptions, equipment damages, and reduced operating hours. Due to difficulties in determining the source of the 
water leaks at the Main Street Garage, the walls inside the store have not been fully repaired as of the writing of this 
report. Consequently, the City’s commercial property manager recommends a landlord concession of 50% of the base rent 
for the initial six months, or approximately $3,600 dollars, distributed evenly across the period. 
89 of 461

--- page 90 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
BUDGET IMPACT:
Rent revenues for the first year will be approximately $11,650 over the next twelve months. Commercial property revenue 
funds the City’s expenses for operations, maintenance and improvement to the Downtown parking facilities and are used 
for street cleaning services. This revenue is credited to the Downtown Parking and Maintenance Program in the General 
Fund. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This agreement is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 
15301.)

receive such notice at least three (3) but not more than six (6) months prior to the date that the applicable Option Term would commence, time 
being of the essence. If timely and proper notification of the exercise of an Extension Option is not given by Lessee and/or received by Lessor, such Extension Option 
shall automatically expire. Except as specifically modified, the terms, conditions and provisions of the Lease shall apply during Option Terms but the amount of Rent

Fair Market Value.
(a)
During the Option Term(s) which start(s) on 
, the amount of Rent shall be the amount forecasted to be the fair market rental value of the 
Premises during such Option Term established pursuant to the procedures, terms, assumptions and conditions set forth herein ("Fair Market Value"); provided, 
however, regardless of such Fair Market Value, Base Rent during an Option Term shall not be less than the Base Rent scheduled as of when the prior term expires. 
Starting as of Lessee's exercise of the applicable Extension Option (but not earlier than six (6) months before start of the applicable Option Term), the Parties shall for 
thirty (30) days ("Negotiation Period") attempt to agree upon the Fair Market Value. If during the Negotiation Period the Parties do not agree on the Fair Market 
Value, then the Fair Market Value shall be established pursuant to the procedures set forth herein, which shall be binding.
(b)
Each Party shall, within fifteen (15) days after the end of the Negotiation Period, in writing submit to the other Party such Party's determination of the Fair 
Market Value ("Submitted Value(s)").  If a Party fails to timely provide a Submitted Value, then the other Party's Submitted Value shall be the Fair Market Value.  If 
both Parties timely provide Submitted Values, then each Party shall, within fifteen (15) days after both Parties have exchanged Submitted Values, in writing notify the 
other Party of such Party's selected arbitrator who shall meet the qualifications set forth herein ("Advocate Arbitrator(s)"). Lessor and Lessee may select an Advocate 
Arbitrator who is favorable to such Party's position and may, prior to or after appointment of an Advocate Arbitrator, consult with such Party's Advocate Arbitrator.  If 
a Party fails to timely and properly provide notice of such Party's chosen Advocate Arbitrator, then the other Party's Submitted Value shall be the Fair Market Value.
(c)
If both Parties timely and properly designate Advocate Arbitrators, then such Advocate Arbitrators shall, within fifteen (15) days after their selection, 
choose a third (3rd) neutral arbitrator who shall meet the qualifications set forth herein ("Neutral Arbitrator"). The Neutral Arbitrator shall be engaged jointly by 
Lessor and Lessee. If Advocate Arbitrators fail to agree upon and timely appoint a Neutral Arbitrator, then the President of AIR CRE shall appoint such Neutral 
Arbitrator within fifteen (15) days after request by either Party.  If the President of AIR CRE does not timely appoint the Neutral Arbitrator, then either Party may file

(d)
The Advocate Arbitrators and the Neutral Arbitrator ("Arbitrator(s)") shall be duly licensed real estate brokers or salespersons in good standing in the state 
in which the Premises is located, shall have been active over the five (5) year period before their appointment in the leasing of properties similar to the Premises 
within the general real estate market of the Premises. The Neutral Arbitrator shall additionally not be related to or affiliated with either Party or Advocate Arbitrator, 
and shall not have previously represented in a real estate transaction a Party or anyone related to or affiliated with a Party. All matters to be determined by the 
Arbitrators shall be decided by a majority vote of the Arbitrators, with each Arbitrator having one (1) vote. The Arbitrators may, as the Arbitrators determine, hold 
hearings and require briefs, including market data and additional information.
(e)
Within thirty (30) days after selection of the Neutral Arbitrator, the three Arbitrators shall first reach a decision as to their own independent opinion of the 
Fair Market Value established by taking into account the terms, assumptions and conditions set forth herein ("Arbitrators' Market Value"), then decide which Party's 
Submitted Value is closer in monetary amount to the Arbitrators' Market Value ("Selected Market Value"), then provide the Parties a copy of the Arbitrators' Market 
Value and finally notify the Parties of the Selected Market Value. The Selected Market Value shall be the Fair Market Value. The Arbitrators shall have no right to 
decide a Selected Market Value which is a compromise to (or modification of) the Submitted Values. The decision of the Arbitrators shall be binding upon the Parties. 
The Party whose Submitted Value is not the Selected Market Value shall, within ten (10) days after the Arbitrators decide the Selected Market Value, pay the fees and 
costs of all three (3) Arbitrators.
(f)
If the Fair Market Value has not been established before the start of the applicable Option Term, then Lessee shall continue to pay to Lessor rent in the 
amount payable for the month immediately preceding the start of such Option Term and Lessor's acceptance of such rent shall not waive, adversely affect or prejudice 
the Parties' right to complete establishment of the Fair Market Value or Lessor's right to collect the full amount of the Fair Market Value once the Fair Market Value is 
established. Lessee shall, within ten (10) days after establishment of the Fair Market Value, pay to Lessor any deficiency in rent then due for the Option Term. 
Following establishment of Fair Market Value, the Parties shall, within ten (10) days after request by either Party, sign an amendment to this Lease to confirm the Fair 
Market Value and the expiration date of this Lease, but the Parties' failure to request or to sign such an amendment shall not affect establishment of the Fair Market 
Value or extension of the Lease term.
(g)
The Arbitrators, in deciding the Arbitrators' Market Value, shall take into account rent rates, rent abatements, periodic rent increases, real property taxes, 
insurance premiums and other operating expenses, tenant improvement and other applicable allowances, building services, length of lease term and other factors 
professional real estate brokers and/or appraisers customarily consider in determining fair market rent of property in an arm's length transaction by ready, willing and 
able parties for space of comparable location, size, age, condition, quality, parking, visibility, view, signage and accessibility if the Premises were marketed in a normal 
and customary manner for a reasonable length of time on the open market to be leased to a tenant with financial strength and credit worthiness comparable to 
Lessee and guarantors (if any) of this Lease (as of Lessee's exercise of the Extension Option) for a term comparable to the length of the applicable Option Term and 
used for the Agreed Use (or other reasonably comparable uses). The Arbitrators, in deciding the Arbitrators' Market Value, shall not consider as a comparable 
transaction any of the following: a sublease, lease assignment, lease renewal or extension; lease with a tenant that has equity, is related to or affiliated with the 
landlord; or a lease of space that was subject to a right of first refusal, right of first offer, expansion option or other encumbrances. The Arbitrators, in deciding the 
Arbitrators' Market Value, shall reduce the Fair Market Value on account of Alterations and improvements made by Lessee to the extent the cost thereof was paid 
solely by Lessee (in excess of any applicable improvement allowance, abated rent in lieu of improvement allowance or other consideration provided by Lessor for 
Lessee's improvement of the Premises), shall not reduce the Fair Market Value on account of any real estate brokerage commission savings by Lessor, and shall not 
reduce the Fair Market Value on account of deferred maintenance or repair of the Premises for which Lessee was responsible under the Lease but did not perform.

FROM:

City Manager's Office
MEETING DATE:
August 15, 2022 
SUBJECT:
Bulk Mailing and Printing – Agreements
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve bulk mailing and printing services agreements with: 1) CMG Language Services, LLC DBA ColorPrint; and 2) AMS 
Systems, Inc. DBA AMS Printing, each for an amount not to exceed $150,000 annually;  with each agreement providing for 
two 1-year extension options for up to $150,000 each year, for a total not to exceed amount of $450,000 for each 
agreement; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreements in substantially the form presented and to 
exercise the extension options for each agreement. 
BACKGROUND:
Various departments throughout the City use mail house services for printing, postage, and distribution of messaging to 
the public. Messaging can include construction notification postcards, project updates, community meeting invitations, 
surveys, street-level signs, and any other large-scale announcements that surpass in-house staff’s capacity to produce. 
Printed communications are a key method to disseminate messaging to the public and have been identified through prior 
community surveys as an effective way for residents to receive information from the City. 
The City issued a Request for Proposals in July 2022 and received four responses. AMS Systems, Inc. dba AMS Printing 
(AMS) and CMG Language Services, LLC dba ColorPrint (Colorprint) provided complete responses, and offered competitive 
pricing and quick turnaround times. Both firms have experience as a vendor with the City, and most recently AMS was the 
vendor for the City’s General Plan mailer and ColorPrint was the vendor for the City’s mailer on district elections. 
As turnaround times and pricing may vary, the City proposes entering into separate agreements with each vendor to 
provide greater access to services and price comparisons. Each agreement would include the option to renew for two 
additional 1-year extensions in an amount not to exceed $150,000 per extension.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The costs associated with these contracts are included in the adopted fiscal year 2022-23 budget. All future services under 
the agreements will be included in future departmental budget appropriations covering the term of the agreements.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
These agreements for bulk mailing and printing services are not subject to CEQA review, because it can be seen with 
certainty that there is no possibility that approval of these agreements may have a significant effect on the environment. 
(CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)

SECTION 16 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES 
 
 
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this provision that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.

origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a 
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act. 
 
SECTION 18 - MEDIATION 
 
 
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw. 
 
 
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties. 
 
SECTION 19 - LITIGATION 
 
 
CONTRACTOR shall testify at CITY's request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONTRACTOR's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONTRACTOR, or 
is based upon CONTRACTOR's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONTRACTOR for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONTRACTOR's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.

EXHIBIT B 
 
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS 
 
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE  
 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit 
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit. 
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if Contractor 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease.  
If the contractor maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall be 
entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the contractor. 
Other Insurance Provisions 
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions: 
Additional Insured Status 
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the Contractor; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the Contractor including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the Contractor’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both CG 
20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used). 
Primary Coverage 
For any claims related to this contract, the Contractor’s insurance coverage shall be primary insurance 
as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any insurance or self-
insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or agents shall be 
excess of the Contractor’s insurance and shall not contribute with it. 
Notice of Cancellation 
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City. 
Waiver of Subrogation 
Contractor hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said Contractor 
may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  Contractor 
agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of subrogation, but this 
provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of subrogation 
endorsement from the insurer.   
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions 
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the Contractor to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof of 
103 of 461

--- page 104 ---
Contract for Services with CMG Language Services DBA Colorprint  
Page 9 of 9 
ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within the 
retention.   
Acceptability of Insurers 
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City. 
Verification of Coverage 
Contractor shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies of 
the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the Contractor’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit 
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit. 
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if Contractor 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease.  
If the contractor maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall be 
entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the contractor.

insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or agents shall be

SUBJECT:
Revision of Interim Child Care Fund Guidelines – Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve the revisions of the Interim Child Care Fund Guidelines.
BACKGROUND:
In October 2018, the City Council approved the current Interim Child Care Fund Guidelines. These guidelines responded to 
Council direction integrating both the inclusion of child care discussions in the General Plan Update process and 
established procedures for the use of funds in the Child Care Facilities Fund (CCFF). The “interim” of the guidelines reflect 
any integration of future actions from the General Plan Update. The CCFF revenue is from a developer impact fee and is 
restricted to capital projects that will expand the number of child care spaces within the City. Council concurred that 
flexibility in procedures, processes, and having various options for partnerships for the use of those funds is in the City’s 
best interest. Council’s approval of these guidelines was also an important part of preparing for the January 2019 Notice of 
Funding Availability (NOFA) that invited proposals for childcare development projects.
As that NOFA was the first of the program, feedback for improvements was desired. After completing the NOFA process 
and project selection, staff conducted a survey of the approximate 25 participants about the process and program 
material; seven of those participants were applicants and three projects were approved. Input received from 15 
responding participants as well as some verbal sharing of ideas included, but wasn’t limited to, the need for more specific 
information to be provided to applicants, clear loan processing procedures, and construction requirements that clearly 
includes prevailing wage. The feedback provided key information that has been used to improve processes and develop 
more robust information for child care providers and others, and to inform the updated City’s Interim Child Care Fund 
Guidelines.  
In 2021, the City adopted San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 23.65 (Child Care Development Fee) to broaden Child Care 
Facilities impact fee applicability and state the requirement in the Municipal Code instead of a resolution. Since then, staff 
has determined that the code is in need of updating to clarify its applicability.  In connection with any such code update, 
the Interim Guidelines will be revised accordingly.  
The changes reflected in the revised guidelines provide further clarification of the fee requirements and strengthens the 
loan program process. It provides the primary loan terms for review prior to application and clearly includes the requisite 
of prevailing wage. The experience of the first three projects and the substantial increases of the cost of construction 
informed the suggestion to increase the forgiveness threshold for smaller projects 5-year loans to $200,000 rather than 
$100,000. Specifically, the smallest of the three projects was approved at $100,000 yet the project completed at $140,000, 
the other two were $464,000 and $265,000. A requirement for project applicants to complete a technical property review 
prior to application submittal has also been included to aid staff and the applicant in identifying potential issues that could 
114 of 461

--- page 115 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
impact project viability and budgets.
Approval of this document will allow staff to release revised program materials and the application for loans on an ongoing 
basis while funds are available. These guidelines will be interim until such time any resulting policy development from the 
General Plan Update or as directed by Council has been completed, and the guidelines can be revised and made 
permanent. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Approval of the Guidelines will not directly impact the budget.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
In accordance with CEQA Guidelines section 15378 (b)(5), approval of the Interim Child Care Fund Guidelines is not a 
project subject to CEQA because this is an administrative activity of government that will not result in direct or indirect 
physical changes in the environment.
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

Rev. & Approved – Aug. 2022
City of San Mateo
Child Care Development Fee
Interim Child Care Fund Guidelines
The City of San Mateo recognizes that high quality childcare provides critical support for the economic growth of our 
families and community, and the intellectual and social development of our children. The City is committed to 
prioritizing and enhancing the supply of child care spaces for children of all ages. 
It is the City’s intent to explore any potential opportunities for increasing childcare spaces within the City through 
development partnerships or financial assistance, as legally permitted.  This exploration can take place through 
conversations with planning project applicants, conversation with childcare providers, or any other nonprofit 
childcare related agencies.  
This set of guidelines for the use of the Child Care Development Fund may be implemented through development 
agreements for new construction, development partnerships for reuse/expanded use of existing sites, inclusion in 
projects on City owned properties, and/or financial agreements with existing providers for capital improvements that 
would expand the number of child care spaces.
Revenue generation to this fund is based on applicable developments within the City and will vary over future years 
accordingly.  The Mitigation Fee Act requires the City to identify projects that will use these funds within five (5) 
years of collecting the fees.  Therefore, flexibility in policy application is warranted as there are several variables to 
project readiness and levels of assistance that may be available.
1.
Program Background
A) History: Original fee implementation in 2004; Revised nexus study and ordinance adoption in 2021.
B) Ordinance (copied below for convenience):
Chapter 23.65 Child Care Development Fee
23.65.010 Purpose
The purpose of the childcare development fee is to fund the development of child care facilities in 
order to serve a need created by both commercial and residential development.
23.65.020 Fee
A childcare development impact fee, in an amount established by City Council resolution is imposed 
on all residential and commercial development, including new development, addition of square 
footage to existing development, and tenant improvements to existing structures if those tenant 
improvements require planning approval.
2.
Assisted Project Eligibility
A) Priority should be given to projects that:
1)
Provide the highest number and/or most enduring number of designated spaces for children from 
families with incomes less than 80 percent of the Area Median Income (AMI)
2)
Have the highest levels of project readiness and construction commencement.
B) Types of potential applicants or project partners
1)
For-profit companies and businesses
2)
Nonprofit providers
3)
Faith-based organizations
4)
The City of San Mateo 
5)
Other governmental agencies (i.e. school districts)
C) Types of eligible projects may include but are not necessarily limited to: 
1)
Center acquisition
2)
New construction of center
3)
Tenant improvements to prepare existing structure for child care uses
116 of 461

--- page 117 ---
Att 1 – Revised Interim Child Care Fund Guidelines.pdf
Page 2 of 3
Rev. & Approved – Aug. 2022
4)
Expansion of currently operating center 
5)
Improvements to establish new small family child care home (FCCH), must be owner occupied
6)
Expansion of small FCCH to large FCCH, must be owner occupied.
7)
Center within corporate campus 
8)
Center within new or existing commercial development
9)
Child care within new housing developments
D) Eligible expenses do not include general operating costs, but may include:
1)
Development or construction related costs
2)
Capital equipment
3)
Fixed furnishings
E)
Financial support may be offered through following methods or any combination thereof: 
1)
Loans
2)
Agreements
3.
Project Commitment 
A) Requisites for assistance include, but are not necessarily limited to:
1)
Letter of request to City, including brief project description
2)
Current year budget, start-up and operating budgets, as applicable
3)
Copy of proposed child care center property deed or lease, as applicable
4)
Resolution in support of request from Board of Directors or comparable body for other types of entities, 
agencies, or organizations
5)
Board of Directors list or proprietor curricula vitae, as applicable
6)
Copy of proof of nonprofit status, as applicable
7)
Previous 2 fiscal year’s audited financial statement
8)
Copy of appropriate license or planned schedule for licensing upon facility start up
B) Final fund commitment will be based on, but not limited to, these elements:
1)
Request is appropriate to project size
2)
Demonstration and verification of financial need
3)
Detailed project plan with timeline, site drawings and itemized cost estimate
4)
The depth of affordability of child care spaces met with City assistance
4.
Loans Terms
As noted in the Project Eligibility section, there are multiple ways the City may choose to fund the increase child 
care spaces. Loans are one of the established methods to provide financial assistance. The following provides a 
summary of the loan terms.
A) Signed agreement with the City specifying terms of assistance and remedies of default.
B) The terms of the loan are reflective of the expectation that a child care facility would have a viable business 
for at least ten (10) years.
•
Zero percent (0%) interest
•
Fully deferred / no payments required
•
Forgivability requires borrowers to meet the annual performance requirements
(a) Loan amounts $200,000 or less forgiven at 20% per year, 5-year loan
(b) Loans greater than $200,000 forgiven at 10% per year, 10-year loan 
•
30 years, total or remaining loan principal due if not already forgiven
The template loan documents will be available for review prior to application. Those documents reflect these and 
other standard loan terms, prevailing wage payment requirements for construction (as applicable), loan draw

Rev. & Approved – Aug. 2022
requests from the borrower, and borrower paying vendors directly. Borrowers will be required to submit 
documentation confirming all construction / development has been completed (Certificate of Occupancy) and all 
liens have been released.
C) Loan Security
1)
Executed promissory note and loan agreement, and one of the following:
(a) Secured with Deed of Trust against property
(b) Secured with business and personal assets
2)
City may be willing to subordinate to senior lender as long as total loan to value (LTV) does not exceed 
95%
D) Loan Repayment
1)
Loan due immediately upon cessation of operation as child care center or Family Child Care Home (FCCH)
2)
Loan due upon transfer of business ownership
3)
Loan due immediately upon default of agreement
4)
Fully amortized, no early payment penalty
E)
Loan Modification
1)
If borrower desires to revise loan amount for construction needs or other special circumstances, 
(a) Modification request, includes a description of the reason & money
(b) Staff determines allowability, develops recommendation
(c) Approval obtained based on City’s purchasing policy 
5.
City Staff Roles & Responsibility
A) Planning staff are encouraged to discuss possible child care facility inclusion opportunities with new, large 
development projects.
B) The prospective applicant will arrange with City staff a site visit, or submit materials such as photos, 
drawings, and/or videos that provide sufficient information for staff to conduct a technical property review. 
The prospective applicant will be provided a written summary of staff’s findings, which will identify potential 
issues associated with the site/structure that could impact a project’s ability to meet regulatory 
requirements or could be cost or time intensive. Completion of this step is not an authorization, but a service 
provided to any prospective applicant to aid them in better identifying budget considerations and project 
viability. 
C) City staff will liaison with 4Cs-Child Care Coordinating Council, Build Up for San Mateo County, and/or other 
childcare related agencies, to identify eligible providers and potential expansion or development 
opportunities.
D) City staff will discuss development agreement options with potential partners.
E)
City staff will administer funds.
F)
City staff is responsible for monitoring compliance of terms of agreement and initiate action for 
noncompliance as delineated in signed terms of agreement.
6.
Reporting Requisites
A) Borrower / partner will be required to provide reports to City as defined in loan or development agreement.
1)
Reporting may include, but not be limited to the following:
(a) Proof of current insurance and license
(b) Number of total child care spaces
(c) Number of affordable/subsidized spaces
(d) Submittal of annual financial statement

SUBJECT:
East Hillsdale Park Construction Drawings – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with Callander Associates Landscape Architecture (CALA) to provide professional design 
refinement, construction document preparation, bid assistance, and construction observation services for East Hillsdale 
Park in the amount of $167,380 with a contingency of $15,000 and authorize the Parks and Recreation Director to execute 
the agreement in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
In February 2020, a neighborhood survey was conducted to obtain input as to the rehabilitation of East Hillsdale Park. The 
park and playground had been largely unrenovated since the late 1990's and as a result needed major work to bring the 
park and playground facilities to current standards in terms of playground equipment and accessibility. In the two years 
that have passed since the initial survey, the Parks and Recreation Department, with numerous public outreach events, has 
arrived at a design for the playground and associated works for the park such as repaving the perimeter path, landscaping, 
lighting, and other park infrastructure. 
In April 2022, a Request for Proposals (RFP) for professional design refinement, construction document preparation, bid 
assistance, and construction observation services was issued prior to construction bids being sought. Of the four proposals 
submitted, staff determined that CALA was the best value for the city, submitting a proposal of $160,614, which was the 
lowest overall bid. Due to additional electrical plan and detail requirements, CALA refined their bid to $167,380. After 
additional review, it was concluded that CALA was still the lowest overall bid. Competing bids ranged from $177,028 
through to $238,200.
Callander Associates Landscape Architecture, Inc.
$167,380
Gates & Associates
$177,028
SSA Landscape Architects, Inc. $181,601
Verde Design, Inc.
$238,200
A contingency of $15,000 (approximately 10%) is being requested for reimbursables and potential engineering expenses.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The costs for the reconstruction and rehabilitation of East Hillsdale Park have been budgeted from the Parks and 
Recreation Capital Improvement Fund. Approximately $1.7 million has been set aside and this amount includes the 
Proposition 68 Per Capita Fund Grant of approximately $241,821, claimable upon completion.

mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be agreed 
to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one name from 
mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and Conciliation 
Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation and 
making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once commenced by 
a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but not more than 60 
days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

SCOPE OF SERVICES
SCOPE OF WORK 
We have prepared the following detailed scope of work based upon the one found within the RFP 
and our project delivery experience. It is obvious that a lot of time and critical thought was put into the 
RFP scope and its level of detail provides a clear picture of the city’s expectations. We have included 
all tasks and specifics from the RFP in the below scope of work while adding a few additional tasks 
and refinements to the language to further expand on our approach, methodology, and to highlight 
unique aspects of our team. By maintaining the same level of detail this confirms our commitment to 
the project and the level of detail you require, allows you to simply include this as an attachment to 
the contract, and reduces your effort in preparing those contract documents.
To assist you in these efforts, we would propose to complete the following tasks in chronological order. 
The items shown in bold-face italics are documents that we would prepare as part of our tasks.
TASK I: PRELIMINARY ENGINEERING INVESTIGATION
1.A.  Site Reconnaissance: With topographic survey in hand, visit site to become familiar with and 
document existing site conditions. Photograph site for studio and presentation purposes. 
Coordinate meeting with Park Maintenance Division staff to confirm existing irrigation system 
components (backflow, controller, valves, QVC’s and rotor heads, in place as needed). 
1.B.  Kick-off Meeting: Meet with City staff to discuss design objectives, park issues, key schedule 
milestones, and obtain input. Based upon input, develop a detailed work plan/schedule through 
construction and clarify roles and responsibilities of both City staff and consultant’s team. Submit 
one (1) draft meeting summary and draft work plan/schedule (in 8 1/2”x11” format) within one 
week of the meeting and, upon City staff review, resubmit final work plan schedule and final 
meeting summary. 
1.C.  Base Data: Review existing information from staff including topographical survey prepared by 
Wilsey-Ham Engineers, and Geotechnical / Environmental Soil Report prepared by Geocon 
Consultant’s Inc. Submit any requests for clarification in a summary memo. 
1.D.  Arborist Services: CALA is proposing to utilize our own in-house ISA certified arborist who is also 
our proposed construction manager. This approach ensures the best possible integration of 
requirements and recommendations into the plans as well as monitoring during construction. 
Proposed services include; 
1)  Site Visit: Utilizing the provided topographic survey and preliminary site plan, arborist will 
conduct a site reconnaissance to document location, species, and size (DSH), to visually 
assess the condition of existing trees, review the existing site conditions and to review the 
relationship of trees to the proposed improvements. The arborist will tag all heritage trees 
with a metal tree tag and number and photograph the trees for inclusion in the arborist 
report. 
127 of 461

--- page 128 ---
Professional Services
Page 8 of 24
Rev 5/22
2)  Arborist Report: Prepare an initial arborist report that identifies all heritage trees (botanical and 
common name) within the project limits being impacted by the proposed improvements, 
tree size in terms of trunk diameter and tree canopy per established standards, condition 
of each heritage tree, the impacts of the proposed site plan on the trees, any removal 
recommendations for unhealthy trees and trees that will be severely impacted, tree 
protection measures for all other heritage trees that will be impacted by all proposed site 
improvements throughout the construction period. Such tree protection measures shall 
include but not be limited to defining the Tree Protection Zone (TPZ) around such trees, 
temporary protective fencing, mulching, feeding and root/limb pruning as required and 
review of all plans prepared by all consultants and providing input regarding design and/
or construction solutions to further protect trees as needed. Submit one (1) pdf copy of 
arborist report in 8.5x11/11x17 format as required to City.
3)  Tree Survey: Based on the arborist’s findings and recommendations, prepare a tree survey
on a single sheet that shows the location, canopy, species, and DSH of trees proposed to 
be removed and retained.
4)  Plan Review: Be involved during the site design plan preparation to understand the 
location of the proposed improvements including replacement of existing pathways and 
curbs, grading and drainage work, and all other proposed site improvements and to make 
recommendations concerning design solutions and construction methods that will minimize 
the impact on Heritage Trees that are of reasonable health and worth saving. Review 
plans related to work within the trees TPZ and provide recommendations for optimal tree 
preservation.
1.E.  Stormwater Analysis: Analyze if the current project design meets C3 and C6 Stormwater 
Requirements and fill out the C3 and C6 Development Review Checklist.  Incorporate any 
requirements and design changes, and submit all required documentation, as part of subsequent 
design submittals.
1.F.  Design Development Submittal: Prepare the design development submittal package documents 
using the latest AutoCAD version. Provide one (1) PDF copy for City staff review. Plans shall be 
at minimum 20 scale, prepared on 30”x48” format sheets, and include city standard title blocks. 
Design development submittal package will include the following:
1)  Existing Conditions Plan: including photos of existing conditions. 
2)  Demolition Plan
3)  Site Plan: including the following;
•  Existing heritage trees with tree numbers keyed to arborist report, protective fencing / 
TPZ zone and tree protection notes based on recommendations from arborist report.
•  New improvements including renovation or replacement of pathways, concrete 
128 of 461

Rev 5/22
curbs, proposed play area and related improvements, and new site furnishings.
•  Limits of areas subject to site disruption and identification of final improvements.
4)  Grading & Drainage Plans (Wilsey Ham): With their experience preparing the site topographic 
survey, Wilsey Ham will have an intimate understanding of the site, existing infrastructure, 
and grading issues which will jump start their plan development. Grading and drainage 
plans will include the following;
•  Preliminary grading and drainage information including existing and proposed 
contours at 0.5’ intervals along with critical spot elevations, new and existing catch 
basins and drain lines, including proposed invert and rim elevations and other required 
utility lines (domestic water line / drain line for dog drinking fountain and water bottle 
filling station. 
•  Grading cut and fill calculations to determine the amount of excavated soil to be 
used on site vs would be off-hauled. Design should attempt to avoid off-hauling to the 
greatest extent possible.
•  C3 and C6 forms, documentation and calculations.
•  Additional plans and documentation to meet the C3 and C6 requirements as needed.
5)  Play Area Illustrations: Work with Miracle/Hags to update play area designs based upon 
community feedback expressed at the Park and Recreation Commission meeting. Miracle/
Hags to prepare updated play area illustrations in color with updated play equipment 
design modifications and play area surfacing.  Illustrations shall be 30”x48” format and 
incorporated into overall design submittal.
6)   Image Board: Prepare an image board with notations and pictures of proposed site 
furnishings in color including picnic tables, benches, water bottle filling stations, light 
fixtures, dog drinking fountain, and City Standard trash / recycling enclosures.  Include
recommended colors. Image board shall be 30”x48” format and incorporated into overall 
design submittal.
7)   Preliminary Construction Staging: Develop a preliminary construction staging plan to 
illustrate proposed phasing of improvements so that a portion, or portions of the park, can 
be publicly accessible from certain alley way entries at different times. CALA will reach out 
to a couple contractors to vet options. This will be a preliminary plan and should be subject 
to review and modification when contractor is selected.  We would also recommend 
before finalizing this, and including it within the project plans and specifications, that the 
city reviews this (along with the revised play area plan) with the community to gather input. 
Construction staging plan shall be 30”x48” format and incorporated into overall design 
submittal.
8)   Cost Estimate: Develop a detailed preliminary estimate of probable construction costs for 
all improvements. Estimate shall also include costs associated with a 60-calendar day sod

establishment period and estimating/inflation contingency to the anticipated bid date of 
June 30, 2023. Cost estimate shall be in 8.5” x 11” format.
1.G.  Review Meeting: Meet with City staff to review the design development submittal package and 
identify any required refinements.  Prepare meeting summary documenting decisions made 
during the meeting.
1.H.  Design Development Submittal Revisions: Based on comments received by the city, revise the 
design development submittal package. Submit one (1) pdf copy to City. Any subsequent 
comments received will be incorporated into the construction and bid documents.
TASK 2: CONSTRUCTION AND BID DOCUMENTS
2.A.  Construction Documents- 90% Plans, Specifications and Estimate (PS&E’s): Based on the approval 
of the documents developed in Task 1, the results of public input, and staff direction prepare 
construction documents to a 90% level of completion. Submit one (1) pdf copy to the City for 
review. All plan sheets shall be 30”x48” format, drawn at a minimum of 20 Scale showing north 
arrow/scale, and shall be overlaid onto the topographic survey reduced in tone as required 
for clarity. Plans shall include a city standard title block containing information such as sheet 
number / total number of sheets, sheet title, name of project, date of submittal, and scale of 
plan. Submittal shall include the following: 
1)  Cover Sheet: Including title of project, site address, submittal level (90%, 100%, Final) and 
date of submittal, table of contents, identification of the City of San Mateo as the owner, 
listing entire Consultant Team with address and phone number, vicinity map showing 
location of project and a larger scale location map showing site and approved truck 
route(s) (to be provided by City), project description, listing of governing codes that the 
plans comply with, list of abbreviations as required, and survey benchmark information as 
required.
•  Cover sheet should also include diagrammatic construction phasing plan and 
notes that describe required signage and notifications to the community regarding 
schedule and construction operations.
2)  Existing Conditions Plan: Plan shall show existing survey information, existing known utilities, 
tree trunk and canopy locations, and a legend as required. 
3)  Demolition & Tree Protection Plan: including the following;
•  All tree trunk locations, canopies, Tree Protection Zones (TPZ), and trunks with reference 
numbers to a listing of Heritage Trees botanical and common names of tree, trunk size, if tree is to be 
saved or removed, and required tree protection fencing. Include notes that described tree protection 
fencing and other measures that should be implemented /complied with prior to and during construction. 
•  Site demolition and preservation notes and descriptions of those areas and items to

4)  Erosion and Sediment Control Plan (Wilsey Ham): including the following;
•  Designations and locations of all erosion and sediment control features such as

5)  Grading and Drainage & Utility Plan and Details (Wilsey Ham): including the following;
•  All proposed flat work including paving, curbing and soft scaped areas. 
•  Existing finished grade contours per the topographical survey and proposed finished 
grade contours at 0.5 foot maximum intervals. Provide subgrade contours for play 
area at maximum 0.5 foot intervals. 
•  Spot elevations: 
o At a maximum of 25 foot on center and at all changes in direction along edges 
of all flat work including asphalt and concrete paving, curbing.
o At all high and low points and at all grade breaks in areas to be surfaced 
including asphalt and concrete paving, play area surfacing, and curbing. 
o At all rim elevations for catch basins, area drains, and manholes. 
o At all invert elevations for catch basins, area drains, cleanouts, manholes and 
sold and perforated drain lines. 
•  Directional flow arrows within all paved areas with percentage of flow indications. 
•  Limits of grading and where existing contours meet existing contours. 
•  All existing and proposed drainage improvements such as storm lines (solid and 
perforated) catch basins, area drains, cleanouts and other proposed or required 
improvements.

elements including benches, water bottle filling stations, picnic tables, trash enclosure, dog 
drinking fountain, play equipment and all other new site elements as required.

to the contractor. Include an enlargement plan as required to describe the play area 
improvements Provide a construction materials schedule that further describes each type 
of flatwork, paving materials, and all site elements including site furnishings including any 
detail number reference as applicable. Pertinent information about the manufacturer and/
or supplier, model number, finish/texture, color, etc. will be included in the specifications.

9)  Construction Details: Provide construction details as required for all site improvements, 
based on information within the Geotechnical report to be provided by the city. The site 
improvements include but are not limited to: 
•  Asphalt pavement, concrete paving and curbing, header boards.
 
•  Section details for all site furnishing including, benches, picnic tables, trash and 
recycling enclosures, water bottle filling station, dog drinking fountain, permanent 
grant signage, temporary construction signage based on input from City.
 
•  Play equipment plans and structural calculations to be provided by the play 
equipment manufacturer.
 
•  Play area surfacing details including full section depth. 
10)  Irrigation Plan: Provide plan, details, notes and other information as required for irrigation 
system including the following;
 
•  Replacement of the rotor system in the northern lawn area including remote control 
valves, boxes, mainline, laterals and LV wire. Upgrade of system for the remaining 
areas of park shall be undertaken by City crews at a later date except as noted 
below. 
•  Replacement of existing transite irrigation mainline with new PVC mainline. 
•  Replace and upgrade the existing irrigation control system for the entire park to 
a Calsense system with communication to the existing centralized computer via 
antenna or approved communication cable to yard as determined by city. Upgrade 
system with a master valve and flow sensor. 
•  All irrigation design and components shall conform to the city’s Park Irrigation 
Standards Manual.
•  The new irrigation system shall comply with municipal code SMMC 23.73 Water 
Conservation Landscaping. The drawings shall include: 
o All water budget calculations including a hydro-zone information table, 
maximum applied water allowance (MAWA) table, and an estimated total 
water use (ETWU) table. 
o An irrigation watering schedule table that identifies for each valve, type of 
irrigation water outlet (rotor, spray head, stream spray, bubbler, drip) the type 
of plant material irrigated, the time in minutes run time per cycle of each 
valve, cycles run per day, number of days per month that cycles are run, the 
total number of minutes run for each valve per month and year and total 
number of gallons of water used each month and year.

TASK 3: BID AND CONSTRUCTION SUPPORT
3.A.  Bidding Assistance: During the bidding period, respond to questions from the bidders, to prepare 
verbiage for addenda and if required supporting drawings and/or attachments as needed. 
This item will be paid for on a time and material basis. Assume up to 24 hours for this service. 
3.B.  Construction Assistance: During the construction period, perform the following tasks when 
called upon by the City: 
1)  Attend pre-construction meeting. Our construction manager/arborist would be in 
attendance to review overall tree protection requirements.
2)  Attend meetings to assist in resolving construction issues related to the design and to
prepare and submit follow up summary. Assume up to three (3) meetings.
3)  Periodic site visits to observe how the progress of construction conforms to the construction 
documents and to prepare and submit follow up observation reports. Assume up to four 
(4) site visits.
 
4)  Assist in the preparation of proposal requests and change orders including any needed 
attachments.
 
5)  Attend site inspection prior to beginning the plant establishment period and again upon 
the completion of plant establishment period and prepare and submit follow up report.
 
6)  Review submittals including any shop drawings prepared by the contractor. Submit one 
(1) pdf copy of submittal signed reviewed stamp indicating result of review and along with 
any additional clarifying information. 
3.C.  Record Drawings:  Prepare final record drawings using latest AutoCAD version based on as-built 
drawings and information prepared by the contractor, change orders, and other site changes 
from the construction documents per the requirements of the of the specifications. Submit one 
(1) pdf copy and one (1) AutoCad copy of record drawings and information to City.

3.D.  Project Archive: Proceed to package all electronic materials prepared, scan key paper

4. ADDITIONAL PROVISIONS:
4.A.  In coordination with the City’s Public Works Lighting Operation and Maintenance Division and the 
City’s Park and Recreation Department work to:
1) Identify the light fixture specifications that best fits with the appearance of existing lights in the 
park. 
2) Research and present two additional alternative lighting fixtures that are in keeping with the 
appearance of the existing park lights that may not be an acorn fixture in an effort to reduce glare 
or backlight from the lights into the neighbors’ yards.  Presentation shall include backup on how 
effective each of the lighting fixtures are in reducing said glare or backlight.
4.B.  The new lights for the play areas shall include dimmers so the lights could be dimmed after the park 
closes.
4.C.  The consultant shall provide plans, details, structural calc's and other information as required to
obtain building / electrical permit(s) from the City of San Mateo for: 
1) The additional park lights for the new play areas including foundation, the modification of the 
existing light poles to include house side shields and for the service panel.  
2) The preparation of an existing photometric plan that encompasses.
•
The proposed play areas including the adjacent picnic table area.
•
The portion of the existing perimeter pathways that are within 50 feet of the proposed play 
areas.
•
The existing pathway that runs east west between the existing perimeter pathways.
•
Areas in the park that are within 10’ of the new play areas and above stated pathways.
The existing photometric plan shall include point by point lighting levels for the areas described 
above on a grid not to exceed 5’ by 5’.  Each point shall report the illuminance to the nearest 0.1 
foot- candle.  Photometric calculations including maximum foot-candles, average foot-candles, 
minimum foot-candles, average to minimum uniformity and maximum to minimum uniformity.  
3) The preparation of a proposed photometric plan resulting from adding lighting within the two 
new play areas including the adjacent picnic table area that will achieve:
•
1 foot candle of average illuminance at ground level.
•
A minimum illuminance of 0.3 foot-candle
•
A uniformity ratio not to exceed 4:1 average to minimum.
•
Light source shall be capable of producing a “bright white” light with a color temperature 
between 3,000K and 4,000K and a color rendering index (CRI) of at least 65. 
Note:  the above achievement criteria closely match the recommendations of IES G-1-16 for 
security lighting in a park.
The plan shall include point by point lighting levels for the same areas of the site described for 
the existing photometric plan and shall include the same grid, report the same illuminance and 
provide the same photometric calculations as described in the existing photometric plan.  
 
4) The inclusion of specifications for fixtures selected for the play areas on the photometric plan.

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 covering 
CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & advertising 
injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit applies, 
either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the general 
aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if CONSULTANT 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury or 
disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall be 
entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on the 
auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf of the 
CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations performed 
by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in connection with 
such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an endorsement to the 
CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 
forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary insurance 
as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any insurance or self-
insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or agents shall be excess 
of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
143 of 461

--- page 144 ---
Professional Services
Page 24 of 24
Rev 5/22
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after thirty 
(30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.
Waiver of Subrogation
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof of 
ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within the 
retention.  
Acceptability of Insurers
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City.
Verification of Coverage
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies of 
the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure to 
obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s obligation 
to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all required insurance 
policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

SUBJECT:
Classification Updates – Police Department
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve: 1) the job specification and salary range for the new classification of Crime and Intelligence 
Analyst; and 2) reallocate 1.0 vacant Management Analyst II position to 1.0 Crime and Intelligence Analyst position in the 
Police Department.
BACKGROUND:
There have been changes in the demands and expectations of the Police Department in recent years that require 
reconsideration in how the Department is structured and staffed to provide optimal services. In recognition of the need for 
an analyst position to analyze criminal activities, identify trends of emerging crime, provide data-driven strategies, and 
help develop effective tactics to reduce crime, the reallocation of a vacant Administrative Assistant position to a 
Management Analyst position was approved by the City Council in March 2022.
Initially, staff believed that the Management Analyst classification was aligned with duties and responsibilities of 
conducting complex crime analyses and producing strategic reports and bulletins to effectively prevent and control crime; 
however, after further evaluation, staff recommends creating a new classification of Crime and Intelligence Analyst, which 
is a specialized classification that captures the required experience, education, knowledge, skills, and abilities necessary to 
successfully perform the essential duties of the position. Consequently, staff wishes to reallocate the vacant Management 
Analyst I-II position to Crime and Intelligence Analyst. It is recommended that the Crime and Intelligence Analyst 
classification be placed in the Management Unit, with a monthly salary range consistent with that of the Management 
Analyst II position at $8,434.11 to $10,054.34. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The new classification of Crime and Intelligence Analyst has the same salary range as the reallocated Management Analyst 
II position, so there will be no budget impact.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
These classification updates are exempt from CEQA review because it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility 
that this activity may have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

Exhibit A
CRIME AND INTELLIGENCE ANALYST
DEFINITION
To perform analysis of the underlying reasons and causes of crime; examine criminal activities to 
identify crime series, patterns and trends; identify investigative leads by determining related cases and 
potential suspects; forecast occurrences of crime; disseminate analytical findings to departmental 
personnel and others; works in special projects outside the area of specialization with considerable 
independence; and to do related work as required.
DISTINGUISHING CHARACTERISTICS
The Crime and Intelligence Analyst is a non-sworn classification primarily responsible for conducting 
complex crime analyses. 
SUPERVISION RECEIVED AND EXERCISED
Receives direction from higher level departmental sworn or administrative management personnel.
EXAMPLES OF DUTIES - Duties may include, but are not limited to, the following:
Analyze and determine trends in criminal activity, identify criminal offenders, trends and patterns of 
crime; convey this information in various formats to appropriate department personnel.
Compile, analyze, correlate and evaluate data from crime, intelligence and arrest reports, law 
enforcement databases and other sources, looking for patterns and trends.
Study offender and victim characteristics and methods of operation.
Analyze dates, times, geography, and environment of crimes to forecast date, time and location of next 
crime in a series.
Summarize and analyze qualitative and quantitative data using calculations such as frequencies, percent 
changes, cross-tabulations, variation and correlation.
Produce complex reports and bulletins for the police department to develop strategies and tactics to 
effectively prevent and control crime.
148 of 461

--- page 149 ---
Manage date available to the public via the department’s data transparency webpage including 
evaluating, recommending and implementing content and design improvements to increase effectiveness 
and efficiency; perform routine updates of data provided on the site.
Assists operations and management personnel in planning the deployment of resources for the 
prevention and suppression of criminal activity
Establish criminal profiles that include prior crimes and criminal relationships as well as criminal 
organizations.  
Develop crime-mapping analysis of geographic data from police reports, calls for service, and other 
sources.
Create and maintain informational databases; use complex databases and software applications such as 
geographic information systems (GIS) mapping tools
Develops and implements work related procedures to satisfy requirements of local, state and federal 
laws
Represent the City in interdepartmental, interagency task forces, community, and professional meetings 
as required; make presentations as necessary.
QUALIFICATIONS
Knowledge of: 
Methods of identifying essential information.
Organizing, maintaining, and retrieving data from electronic files.
Research methods as they apply to crime analysis.
Statistical analysis techniques.
Collecting, interpreting and evaluating narrative and statistical data pertaining to public safety matters 
and translating these results into coherent, well-written reports with effective recommendations.
Data processing to produce bulletins and reports including graphics such as charts, maps, pictures and 
diagrams; electronic matrixes and spreadsheets; statistical formulae including frequency, percentages, 
percentage change, sum, average, standard deviation, regression analysis, forecasting and correlations. 
Planning, organizing and prioritizing responsibilities so that projects and reports are completed in a 
timely and accurate manner
Performing highly complex analyses utilizing current industry standard methodologies.
Federal, state and local laws as they relate to the essential functions of this position.
149 of 461

--- page 150 ---
Using independent reasoning to solve complex problems.
Standard office practices, procedures, methods and equipment.
Specialized computer software, GIS mapping tools and crime analysis applications.
Ability to:
Identify complex problems and review related information to develop and evaluate options and 
implement solutions
Operate personal computer with proficiency including spreadsheet expertise and familiarity with law 
enforcement software.
Perform cross tabulations, create charts and graphs, export objects to other applications
Work with restricted law enforcement documents and highly confidential information
Use logic and reasoning to identify strengths and weaknesses of alternative solutions, conclusions, or 
approaches to problems
Combine separate pieces of information to form specific answers to problems or conclusions
Effectively convey information to others in presentation form and effectively respond to audience 
inquiries
Communication information and ideas in writing and make recommendations in narrative form that are 
objective, succinct, pertinent, articulate and relevant
Be self-motivated, perceiving departmental need and performing analysis on own initiative
Sit at a desk and use a computer and telephone effectively
Establish and maintain cooperative working relationships with those contacted in the course of work.
Attend work and perform duties on a regular and consistent basis.  Ability and willingness to testify in 
court.
Experience and Training Guidelines
Any combination of experience and education that would likely provide the required knowledge and 
abilities is qualifying. A typical way to obtain the knowledge and abilities would be:
Experience:
Two years of progressively responsible experience performing analytical, crime analysis or intelligence 
related work, preferably in a law enforcement agency.
150 of 461

--- page 151 ---
Training:
Equivalent to a Bachelor’s Degree from an accredited college or university with major work in statistical 
analysis, public administration, administration of justice, criminal justice, or a closely related field; OR
Any combination of experience and training which provides the equivalent scope of knowledge, skills, 
and abilities necessary to perform the work.
ADA Special Requirement: 
Essential duties require the following physical abilities and work environment: 
Ability to work in a standard office environment.
License or Certificate:
Possession of a valid Class C California Driver’s License.
Possession of a certification in Crime and Intelligence Analysis from an accredited college or university 
and/or a POST certificate in Advanced Concepts in Criminal Intelligence, at the time of application, are 
highly desirable. 
A valid certification in Crime and Intelligence Analysis within twelve (12) months of appointment is 
required.
Required Special Qualification:
Must successfully complete a thorough law enforcement background investigation.
